## Assistant (Build · MiniMax-M2.7 · 14.5s)

_Thinking:_

I found the repo. I can see there's a `skill-judge` skill. Let me fetch its content directly.

**Tool: github_get_file_contents**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "owner": "softaworks",
  "path": "skills/skill-judge/SKILL.md",
  "repo": "agent-toolkit"
}
```

**Output:**
```
{
  "name": "SKILL.md",
  "path": "skills/skill-judge/SKILL.md",
  "sha": "6d183975ba7369622a635184f1f8bfbaa9075bc0",
  "size": 31029,
  "url": "https://api.github.com/repos/softaworks/agent-toolkit/contents/skills/skill-judge/SKILL.md?ref=main",
  "html_url": "https://github.com/softaworks/agent-toolkit/blob/main/skills/skill-judge/SKILL.md",
  "git_url": "https://api.github.com/repos/softaworks/agent-toolkit/git/blobs/6d183975ba7369622a635184f1f8bfbaa9075bc0",
  "download_url": "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/softaworks/agent-toolkit/main/skills/skill-judge/SKILL.md",
  "type": "file",
  "content": "---\nname: skill-judge\ndescription: Evaluate Agent Skill design quality against official specifications and best practices. Use when reviewing, auditing, or improving SKILL.md files and skill packages. Provides multi-dimensional scoring and actionable improvement suggestions.\n---\n\n# Skill Judge\n\nEvaluate Agent Skills against official specifications and patterns derived from 17+ official examples.\n\n---\n\n## Core Philosophy\n\n### What is a Skill?\n\nA Skill is NOT a tutorial. A Skill is a **knowledge externalization mechanism**.\n\nTraditional AI knowledge is locked in model parameters. To teach new capabilities:\n```\nTraditional: Collect data → GPU cluster → Train → Deploy new version\nCost: $10,000 - $1,000,000+\nTimeline: Weeks to months\n```\n\nSkills change this:\n```\nSkill: Edit SKILL.md → Save → Takes effect on next invocation\nCost: $0\nTimeline: Instant\n```\n\nThis is the paradigm shift from \"training AI\" to \"educating AI\" — like a hot-swappable LoRA adapter that requires no training. You edit a Markdown file in natural language, and the model's behavior changes.\n\n### The Core Formula\n\n> **Good Skill = Expert-only Knowledge − What Claude Already Knows**\n\nA Skill's value is measured by its **knowledge delta** — the gap between what it provides and what the model already knows.\n\n- **Expert-only knowledge**: Decision trees, trade-offs, edge cases, anti-patterns, domain-specific thinking frameworks — things that take years of experience to accumulate\n- **What Claude already knows**: Basic concepts, standard library usage, common programming patterns, general best practices\n\nWhen a Skill explains \"what is PDF\" or \"how to write a for-loop\", it's compressing knowledge Claude already has. This is **token waste** — context window is a public resource shared with system prompts, conversation history, other Skills, and user requests.\n\n### Tool vs Skill\n\n| Concept | Essence | Function | Example |\n|---------|---------|----------|---------|\n| **Tool** | What model CAN do | Execute actions | bash, read_file, write_file, WebSearch |\n| **Skill** | What model KNOWS how to do | Guide decisions | PDF processing, MCP building, frontend design |\n\nTools define capability boundaries — without bash tool, model can't execute commands.\nSkills inject knowledge — without frontend-design Skill, model produces generic UI.\n\n**The equation**:\n```\nGeneral Agent + Excellent Skill = Domain Expert Agent\n```\n\nSame Claude model, different Skills loaded, becomes different experts.\n\n### Three Types of Knowledge in Skills\n\nWhen evaluating, categorize each section:\n\n| Type | Definition | Treatment |\n|------|------------|-----------|\n| **Expert** | Claude genuinely doesn't know this | Must keep — this is the Skill's value |\n| **Activation** | Claude knows but may not think of | Keep if brief — serves as reminder |\n| **Redundant** | Claude definitely knows this | Should delete — wastes tokens |\n\nThe art of Skill design is maximizing Expert content, using Activation sparingly, and eliminating Redundant ruthlessly.\n\n---\n\n## Evaluation Dimensions (120 points total)\n\n### D1: Knowledge Delta (20 points) — THE CORE DIMENSION\n\nThe most important dimension. Does the Skill add genuine expert knowledge?\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-5 | Explains basics Claude knows (what is X, how to write code, standard library tutorials) |\n| 6-10 | Mixed: some expert knowledge diluted by obvious content |\n| 11-15 | Mostly expert knowledge with minimal redundancy |\n| 16-20 | Pure knowledge delta — every paragraph earns its tokens |\n\n**Red flags** (instant score ≤5):\n- \"What is [basic concept]\" sections\n- Step-by-step tutorials for standard operations\n- Explaining how to use common libraries\n- Generic best practices (\"write clean code\", \"handle errors\")\n- Definitions of industry-standard terms\n\n**Green flags** (indicators of high knowledge delta):\n- Decision trees for non-obvious choices (\"when X fails, try Y because Z\")\n- Trade-offs only an expert would know (\"A is faster but B handles edge case C\")\n- Edge cases from real-world experience\n- \"NEVER do X because [non-obvious reason]\"\n- Domain-specific thinking frameworks\n\n**Evaluation questions**:\n1. For each section, ask: \"Does Claude already know this?\"\n2. If explaining something, ask: \"Is this explaining TO Claude or FOR Claude?\"\n3. Count paragraphs that are Expert vs Activation vs Redundant\n\n---\n\n### D2: Mindset + Appropriate Procedures (15 points)\n\nDoes the Skill transfer expert **thinking patterns** along with **necessary domain-specific procedures**?\n\nThe difference between experts and novices isn't \"knowing how to operate\" — it's \"how to think about the problem.\" But thinking patterns alone aren't enough when Claude lacks domain-specific procedural knowledge.\n\n**Key distinction**:\n| Type | Example | Value |\n|------|---------|-------|\n| **Thinking patterns** | \"Before designing, ask: What makes this memorable?\" | High — shapes decision-making |\n| **Domain-specific procedures** | \"OOXML workflow: unpack → edit XML → validate → pack\" | High — Claude may not know this |\n| **Generic procedures** | \"Step 1: Open file, Step 2: Edit, Step 3: Save\" | Low — Claude already knows |\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-3 | Only generic procedures Claude already knows |\n| 4-7 | Has domain procedures but lacks thinking frameworks |\n| 8-11 | Good balance: thinking patterns + domain-specific workflows |\n| 12-15 | Expert-level: shapes thinking AND provides procedures Claude wouldn't know |\n\n**What counts as valuable procedures**:\n- Workflows Claude hasn't been trained on (new tools, proprietary systems)\n- Correct ordering that's non-obvious (e.g., \"validate BEFORE packing, not after\")\n- Critical steps that are easy to miss (e.g., \"MUST recalculate formulas after editing\")\n- Domain-specific sequences (e.g., MCP server's 4-phase development process)\n\n**What counts as redundant procedures**:\n- Generic file operations (open, read, write, save)\n- Standard programming patterns (loops, conditionals, error handling)\n- Common library usage that's well-documented\n\n**Expert thinking patterns look like**:\n```markdown\nBefore [action], ask yourself:\n- **Purpose**: What problem does this solve? Who uses it?\n- **Constraints**: What are the hidden requirements?\n- **Differentiation**: What makes this solution memorable?\n```\n\n**Valuable domain procedures look like**:\n```markdown\n### Redlining Workflow (Claude wouldn't know this sequence)\n1. Convert to markdown: `pandoc --track-changes=all`\n2. Map text to XML: grep for text in document.xml\n3. Implement changes in batches of 3-10\n4. Pack and verify: check ALL changes were applied\n```\n\n**Redundant generic procedures look like**:\n```markdown\nStep 1: Open the file\nStep 2: Find the section\nStep 3: Make the change\nStep 4: Save and test\n```\n\n**The test**:\n1. Does it tell Claude WHAT to think about? (thinking patterns)\n2. Does it tell Claude HOW to do things it wouldn't know? (domain procedures)\n\nA good Skill provides both when needed.\n\n---\n\n### D3: Anti-Pattern Quality (15 points)\n\nDoes the Skill have effective NEVER lists?\n\n**Why this matters**: Half of expert knowledge is knowing what NOT to do. A senior designer sees purple gradient on white background and instinctively cringes — \"too AI-generated.\" This intuition for \"what absolutely not to do\" comes from stepping on countless landmines.\n\nClaude hasn't stepped on these landmines. It doesn't know Inter font is overused, doesn't know purple gradients are the signature of AI-generated content. Good Skills must explicitly state these \"absolute don'ts.\"\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-3 | No anti-patterns mentioned |\n| 4-7 | Generic warnings (\"avoid errors\", \"be careful\", \"consider edge cases\") |\n| 8-11 | Specific NEVER list with some reasoning |\n| 12-15 | Expert-grade anti-patterns with WHY — things only experience teaches |\n\n**Expert anti-patterns** (specific + reason):\n```markdown\nNEVER use generic AI-generated aesthetics like:\n- Overused font families (Inter, Roboto, Arial)\n- Cliched color schemes (particularly purple gradients on white backgrounds)\n- Predictable layouts and component patterns\n- Default border-radius on everything\n```\n\n**Weak anti-patterns** (vague, no reasoning):\n```markdown\nAvoid making mistakes.\nBe careful with edge cases.\nDon't write bad code.\n```\n\n**The test**: Would an expert read the anti-pattern list and say \"yes, I learned this the hard way\"? Or would they say \"this is obvious to everyone\"?\n\n---\n\n### D4: Specification Compliance — Especially Description (15 points)\n\nDoes the Skill follow official format requirements? **Special focus on description quality.**\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-5 | Missing frontmatter or invalid format |\n| 6-10 | Has frontmatter but description is vague or incomplete |\n| 11-13 | Valid frontmatter, description has WHAT but weak on WHEN |\n| 14-15 | Perfect: comprehensive description with WHAT, WHEN, and trigger keywords |\n\n**Frontmatter requirements**:\n- `name`: lowercase, alphanumeric + hyphens only, ≤64 characters\n- `description`: **THE MOST CRITICAL FIELD** — determines if skill gets used at all\n\n---\n\n**Why description is THE MOST IMPORTANT field**:\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│  SKILL ACTIVATION FLOW                                              │\n│                                                                     │\n│  User Request → Agent sees ALL skill descriptions → Decides which  │\n│                 (only descriptions, not bodies!)     to activate    │\n│                                                                     │\n│  If description doesn't match → Skill NEVER gets loaded            │\n│  If description is vague → Skill might not trigger when it should  │\n│  If description lacks keywords → Skill is invisible to the Agent   │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n**The brutal truth**: A Skill with perfect content but poor description is **useless** — it will never be activated. The description is the **only chance** to tell the Agent \"use me in these situations.\"\n\n---\n\n**Description must answer THREE questions**:\n\n1. **WHAT**: What does this Skill do? (functionality)\n2. **WHEN**: In what situations should it be used? (trigger scenarios)\n3. **KEYWORDS**: What terms should trigger this Skill? (searchable terms)\n\n**Excellent description** (all three elements):\n```yaml\ndescription: \"Comprehensive document creation, editing, and analysis with support\nfor tracked changes, comments, formatting preservation, and text extraction.\nWhen Claude needs to work with professional documents (.docx files) for:\n(1) Creating new documents, (2) Modifying or editing content,\n(3) Working with tracked changes, (4) Adding comments, or any other document tasks\"\n```\n\nAnalysis:\n- WHAT: creation, editing, analysis, tracked changes, comments\n- WHEN: \"When Claude needs to work with... for: (1)... (2)... (3)...\"\n- KEYWORDS: .docx files, tracked changes, professional documents\n\n**Poor description** (missing elements):\n```yaml\ndescription: \"处理文档相关功能\"\n```\n\nProblems:\n- WHAT: vague (\"文档相关功能\" — what specifically?)\n- WHEN: missing (when should Agent use this?)\n- KEYWORDS: missing (no \".docx\", no specific scenarios)\n\n**Another poor example**:\n```yaml\ndescription: \"A helpful skill for various tasks\"\n```\n\nThis is useless — Agent has no idea when to activate it.\n\n---\n\n**Description quality checklist**:\n- [ ] Lists specific capabilities (not just \"helps with X\")\n- [ ] Includes explicit trigger scenarios (\"Use when...\", \"When user asks for...\")\n- [ ] Contains searchable keywords (file extensions, domain terms, action verbs)\n- [ ] Specific enough that Agent knows EXACTLY when to use it\n- [ ] Includes scenarios where this skill MUST be used (not just \"can be used\")\n\n---\n\n### D5: Progressive Disclosure (15 points)\n\nDoes the Skill implement proper content layering?\n\nSkill loading has three layers:\n```\nLayer 1: Metadata (always in memory)\n         Only name + description\n         ~100 tokens per skill\n\nLayer 2: SKILL.md Body (loaded after triggering)\n         Detailed guidelines, code examples, decision trees\n         Ideal: < 500 lines\n\nLayer 3: Resources (loaded on demand)\n         scripts/, references/, assets/\n         No limit\n```\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-5 | Everything dumped in SKILL.md (>500 lines, no structure) |\n| 6-10 | Has references but unclear when to load them |\n| 11-13 | Good layering with MANDATORY triggers present |\n| 14-15 | Perfect: decision trees + explicit triggers + \"Do NOT Load\" guidance |\n\n**For Skills WITH references directory**, check Loading Trigger Quality:\n\n| Trigger Quality | Characteristics |\n|-----------------|-----------------|\n| Poor | References listed at end, no loading guidance |\n| Mediocre | Some triggers but not embedded in workflow |\n| Good | MANDATORY triggers in workflow steps |\n| Excellent | Scenario detection + conditional triggers + \"Do NOT Load\" |\n\n**The loading problem**:\n```\nLoading too little ◄─────────────────────────────────► Loading too much\n- References sit unused                    - Wastes context space\n- Agent doesn't know when to load          - Irrelevant info dilutes key content\n- Knowledge is there but never accessed    - Unnecessary token overhead\n```\n\n**Good loading trigger** (embedded in workflow):\n```markdown\n### Creating New Document\n\n**MANDATORY - READ ENTIRE FILE**: Before proceeding, you MUST read\n[`docx-js.md`](docx-js.md) (~500 lines) completely from start to finish.\n**NEVER set any range limits when reading this file.**\n\n**Do NOT load** `ooxml.md` or `redlining.md` for this task.\n```\n\n**Bad loading trigger** (just listed):\n```markdown\n## References\n- docx-js.md - for creating documents\n- ooxml.md - for editing\n- redlining.md - for tracking changes\n```\n\n**For simple Skills** (no references, <100 lines): Score based on conciseness and self-containment.\n\n---\n\n### D6: Freedom Calibration (15 points)\n\nIs the level of specificity appropriate for the task's fragility?\n\nDifferent tasks need different levels of constraint. This is about matching freedom to fragility.\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-5 | Severely mismatched (rigid scripts for creative tasks, vague for fragile ops) |\n| 6-10 | Partially appropriate, some mismatches |\n| 11-13 | Good calibration for most scenarios |\n| 14-15 | Perfect freedom calibration throughout |\n\n**The freedom spectrum**:\n\n| Task Type | Should Have | Why | Example Skill |\n|-----------|-------------|-----|---------------|\n| Creative/Design | High freedom | Multiple valid approaches, differentiation is value | frontend-design |\n| Code review | Medium freedom | Principles exist but judgment required | code-review |\n| File format operations | Low freedom | One wrong byte corrupts file, consistency critical | docx, xlsx, pdf |\n\n**High freedom** (text-based instructions):\n```markdown\nCommit to a BOLD aesthetic direction. Pick an extreme: brutally minimal,\nmaximalist chaos, retro-futuristic, organic natural...\n```\n\n**Medium freedom** (pseudocode or parameterized):\n```markdown\nReview priority:\n1. Security vulnerabilities (must fix)\n2. Logic errors (must fix)\n3. Performance issues (should fix)\n4. Maintainability (optional)\n```\n\n**Low freedom** (specific scripts, exact steps):\n```markdown\n**MANDATORY**: Use exact script in `scripts/create-doc.py`\nParameters: --title \"X\" --author \"Y\"\nDo NOT modify the script.\n```\n\n**The test**: Ask \"if Agent makes a mistake, what's the consequence?\"\n- High consequence → Low freedom\n- Low consequence → High freedom\n\n---\n\n### D7: Pattern Recognition (10 points)\n\nDoes the Skill follow an established official pattern?\n\nThrough analyzing 17 official Skills, we identified 5 main design patterns:\n\n| Pattern | ~Lines | Key Characteristics | Example | When to Use |\n|---------|--------|---------------------|---------|-------------|\n| **Mindset** | ~50 | Thinking > technique, strong NEVER list, high freedom | frontend-design | Creative tasks requiring taste |\n| **Navigation** | ~30 | Minimal SKILL.md, routes to sub-files | internal-comms | Multiple distinct scenarios |\n| **Philosophy** | ~150 | Two-step: Philosophy → Express, emphasizes craft | canvas-design | Art/creation requiring originality |\n| **Process** | ~200 | Phased workflow, checkpoints, medium freedom | mcp-builder | Complex multi-step projects |\n| **Tool** | ~300 | Decision trees, code examples, low freedom | docx, pdf, xlsx | Precise operations on specific formats |\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-3 | No recognizable pattern, chaotic structure |\n| 4-6 | Partially follows a pattern with significant deviations |\n| 7-8 | Clear pattern with minor deviations |\n| 9-10 | Masterful application of appropriate pattern |\n\n**Pattern selection guide**:\n\n| Your Task Characteristics | Recommended Pattern |\n|---------------------------|---------------------|\n| Needs taste and creativity | Mindset (~50 lines) |\n| Needs originality and craft quality | Philosophy (~150 lines) |\n| Has multiple distinct sub-scenarios | Navigation (~30 lines) |\n| Complex multi-step project | Process (~200 lines) |\n| Precise operations on specific format | Tool (~300 lines) |\n\n---\n\n### D8: Practical Usability (15 points)\n\nCan an Agent actually use this Skill effectively?\n\n| Score | Criteria |\n|-------|----------|\n| 0-5 | Confusing, incomplete, contradictory, or untested guidance |\n| 6-10 | Usable but with noticeable gaps |\n| 11-13 | Clear guidance for common cases |\n| 14-15 | Comprehensive coverage including edge cases and error handling |\n\n**Check for**:\n- **Decision trees**: For multi-path scenarios, is there clear guidance on which path to take?\n- **Code examples**: Do they actually work? Or are they pseudocode that breaks?\n- **Error handling**: What if the main approach fails? Are fallbacks provided?\n- **Edge cases**: Are unusual but realistic scenarios covered?\n- **Actionability**: Can Agent immediately act, or needs to figure things out?\n\n**Good usability** (decision tree + fallback):\n```markdown\n| Task | Primary Tool | Fallback | When to Use Fallback |\n|------|-------------|----------|----------------------|\n| Read text | pdftotext | PyMuPDF | Need layout info |\n| Extract tables | camelot-py | tabula-py | camelot fails |\n\n**Common issues**:\n- Scanned PDF: pdftotext returns blank → Use OCR first\n- Encrypted PDF: Permission error → Use PyMuPDF with password\n```\n\n**Poor usability** (vague):\n```markdown\nUse appropriate tools for PDF processing.\nHandle errors properly.\nConsider edge cases.\n```\n\n---\n\n## NEVER Do When Evaluating\n\n- **NEVER** give high scores just because it \"looks professional\" or is well-formatted\n- **NEVER** ignore token waste — every redundant paragraph should result in deduction\n- **NEVER** let length impress you — a 43-line Skill can outperform a 500-line Skill\n- **NEVER** skip mentally testing the decision trees — do they actually lead to correct choices?\n- **NEVER** forgive explaining basics with \"but it provides helpful context\"\n- **NEVER** overlook missing anti-patterns — if there's no NEVER list, that's a significant gap\n- **NEVER** assume all procedures are valuable — distinguish domain-specific from generic\n- **NEVER** undervalue the description field — poor description = skill never gets used\n- **NEVER** put \"when to use\" info only in the body — Agent only sees description before loading\n\n---\n\n## Evaluation Protocol\n\n### Step 1: First Pass — Knowledge Delta Scan\n\nRead SKILL.md completely and for each section ask:\n> \"Does Claude already know this?\"\n\nMark each section as:\n- **[E] Expert**: Claude genuinely doesn't know this — value-add\n- **[A] Activation**: Claude knows but brief reminder is useful — acceptable\n- **[R] Redundant**: Claude definitely knows this — should be deleted\n\nCalculate rough ratio: E:A:R\n- Good Skill: >70% Expert, <20% Activation, <10% Redundant\n- Mediocre Skill: 40-70% Expert, high Activation\n- Bad Skill: <40% Expert, high Redundant\n\n### Step 2: Structure Analysis\n\n```\n[ ] Check frontmatter validity\n[ ] Count total lines in SKILL.md\n[ ] List all reference files and their sizes\n[ ] Identify which pattern the Skill follows\n[ ] Check for loading triggers (if references exist)\n```\n\n### Step 3: Score Each Dimension\n\nFor each of the 8 dimensions:\n1. Find specific evidence (quote relevant lines)\n2. Assign score with one-line justification\n3. Note specific improvements if score < max\n\n### Step 4: Calculate Total & Grade\n\n```\nTotal = D1 + D2 + D3 + D4 + D5 + D6 + D7 + D8\nMax = 120 points\n```\n\n**Grade Scale** (percentage-based):\n| Grade | Percentage | Meaning |\n|-------|------------|---------|\n| A | 90%+ (108+) | Excellent — production-ready expert Skill |\n| B | 80-89% (96-107) | Good — minor improvements needed |\n| C | 70-79% (84-95) | Adequate — clear improvement path |\n| D | 60-69% (72-83) | Below Average — significant issues |\n| F | <60% (<72) | Poor — needs fundamental redesign |\n\n### Step 5: Generate Report\n\n```markdown\n# Skill Evaluation Report: [Skill Name]\n\n## Summary\n- **Total Score**: X/120 (X%)\n- **Grade**: [A/B/C/D/F]\n- **Pattern**: [Mindset/Navigation/Philosophy/Process/Tool]\n- **Knowledge Ratio**: E:A:R = X:Y:Z\n- **Verdict**: [One sentence assessment]\n\n## Dimension Scores\n\n| Dimension | Score | Max | Notes |\n|-----------|-------|-----|-------|\n| D1: Knowledge Delta | X | 20 | |\n| D2: Mindset vs Mechanics | X | 15 | |\n| D3: Anti-Pattern Quality | X | 15 | |\n| D4: Specification Compliance | X | 15 | |\n| D5: Progressive Disclosure | X | 15 | |\n| D6: Freedom Calibration | X | 15 | |\n| D7: Pattern Recognition | X | 10 | |\n| D8: Practical Usability | X | 15 | |\n\n## Critical Issues\n[List must-fix problems that significantly impact the Skill's effectiveness]\n\n## Top 3 Improvements\n1. [Highest impact improvement with specific guidance]\n2. [Second priority improvement]\n3. [Third priority improvement]\n\n## Detailed Analysis\n[For each dimension scoring below 80%, provide:\n- What's missing or problematic\n- Specific examples from the Skill\n- Concrete suggestions for improvement]\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Failure Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: The Tutorial\n```\nSymptom: Explains what PDF is, how Python works, basic library usage\nRoot cause: Author assumes Skill should \"teach\" the model\nFix: Claude already knows this. Delete all basic explanations.\n     Focus on expert decisions, trade-offs, and anti-patterns.\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: The Dump\n```\nSymptom: SKILL.md is 800+ lines with everything included\nRoot cause: No progressive disclosure design\nFix: Core routing and decision trees in SKILL.md (<300 lines ideal)\n     Detailed content in references/, loaded on-demand\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: The Orphan References\n```\nSymptom: References directory exists but files are never loaded\nRoot cause: No explicit loading triggers\nFix: Add \"MANDATORY - READ ENTIRE FILE\" at workflow decision points\n     Add \"Do NOT Load\" to prevent over-loading\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: The Checkbox Procedure\n```\nSymptom: Step 1, Step 2, Step 3... mechanical procedures\nRoot cause: Author thinks in procedures, not thinking frameworks\nFix: Transform into \"Before doing X, ask yourself...\"\n     Focus on decision principles, not operation sequences\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: The Vague Warning\n```\nSymptom: \"Be careful\", \"avoid errors\", \"consider edge cases\"\nRoot cause: Author knows things can go wrong but hasn't articulated specifics\nFix: Specific NEVER list with concrete examples and non-obvious reasons\n     \"NEVER use X because [specific problem that takes experience to learn]\"\n```\n\n### Pattern 6: The Invisible Skill\n```\nSymptom: Great content but skill rarely gets activated\nRoot cause: Description is vague, missing keywords, or lacks trigger scenarios\nFix: Description must answer WHAT, WHEN, and include KEYWORDS\n     \"Use when...\" + specific scenarios + searchable terms\n\nExample fix:\nBAD:  \"Helps with document tasks\"\nGOOD: \"Create, edit, and analyze .docx files. Use when working with\n       Word documents, tracked changes, or professional document formatting.\"\n```\n\n### Pattern 7: The Wrong Location\n```\nSymptom: \"When to use this Skill\" section in body, not in description\nRoot cause: Misunderstanding of three-layer loading\nFix: Move all triggering information to description field\n     Body is only loaded AFTER triggering decision is made\n```\n\n### Pattern 8: The Over-Engineered\n```\nSymptom: README.md, CHANGELOG.md, INSTALLATION_GUIDE.md, CONTRIBUTING.md\nRoot cause: Treating Skill like a software project\nFix: Delete all auxiliary files. Only include what Agent needs for the task.\n     No documentation about the Skill itself.\n```\n\n### Pattern 9: The Freedom Mismatch\n```\nSymptom: Rigid scripts for creative tasks, vague guidance for fragile operations\nRoot cause: Not considering task fragility\nFix: High freedom for creative (principles, not steps)\n     Low freedom for fragile (exact scripts, no parameters)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Quick Reference Checklist\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│  SKILL EVALUATION QUICK CHECK                                           │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                                                                         │\n│  KNOWLEDGE DELTA (most important):                                      │\n│    [ ] No \"What is X\" explanations for basic concepts                   │\n│    [ ] No step-by-step tutorials for standard operations                │\n│    [ ] Has decision trees for non-obvious choices                       │\n│    [ ] Has trade-offs only experts would know                           │\n│    [ ] Has edge cases from real-world experience                        │\n│                                                                         │\n│  MINDSET + PROCEDURES:                                                  │\n│    [ ] Transfers thinking patterns (how to think about problems)        │\n│    [ ] Has \"Before doing X, ask yourself...\" frameworks                 │\n│    [ ] Includes domain-specific procedures Claude wouldn't know         │\n│    [ ] Distinguishes valuable procedures from generic ones              │\n│                                                                         │\n│  ANTI-PATTERNS:                                                         │\n│    [ ] Has explicit NEVER list                                          │\n│    [ ] Anti-patterns are specific, not vague                            │\n│    [ ] Includes WHY (non-obvious reasons)                               │\n│                                                                         │\n│  SPECIFICATION (description is critical!):                              │\n│    [ ] Valid YAML frontmatter                                           │\n│    [ ] name: lowercase, ≤64 chars                                       │\n│    [ ] description answers: WHAT does it do?                            │\n│    [ ] description answers: WHEN should it be used?                     │\n│    [ ] description contains trigger KEYWORDS                            │\n│    [ ] description is specific enough for Agent to know when to use     │\n│                                                                         │\n│  STRUCTURE:                                                             │\n│    [ ] SKILL.md < 500 lines (ideal < 300)                               │\n│    [ ] Heavy content in references/                                     │\n│    [ ] Loading triggers embedded in workflow                            │\n│    [ ] Has \"Do NOT Load\" for preventing over-loading                    │\n│                                                                         │\n│  FREEDOM:                                                               │\n│    [ ] Creative tasks → High freedom (principles)                       │\n│    [ ] Fragile operations → Low freedom (exact scripts)                 │\n│                                                                         │\n│  USABILITY:                                                             │\n│    [ ] Decision trees for multi-path scenarios                          │\n│    [ ] Working code examples                                            │\n│    [ ] Error handling and fallbacks                                     │\n│    [ ] Edge cases covered                                               │\n│                                                                         │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n---\n\n## The Meta-Question\n\nWhen evaluating any Skill, always return to this fundamental question:\n\n> **\"Would an expert in this domain, looking at this Skill, say:**\n> **'Yes, this captures knowledge that took me years to learn'?\"**\n\nIf the answer is yes → the Skill has genuine value.\nIf the answer is no → it's compressing what Claude already knows.\n\nThe best Skills are **compressed expert brains** — they take a designer's 10 years of aesthetic accumulation and compress it into 43 lines, or a document expert's operational experience into a 200-line decision tree.\n\nWhat gets compressed must be things Claude doesn't have. Otherwise, it's garbage compression.\n\n---\n\n## Self-Evaluation Note\n\nThis Skill (skill-judge) should itself pass evaluation:\n\n- **Knowledge Delta**: Provides specific evaluation criteria Claude wouldn't generate on its own\n- **Mindset**: Shapes how to think about Skill quality, not just checklist items\n- **Anti-Patterns**: \"NEVER Do When Evaluating\" section with specific don'ts\n- **Specification**: Valid frontmatter with comprehensive description\n- **Progressive Disclosure**: Self-contained, no external references needed\n- **Freedom**: Medium freedom appropriate for evaluation task\n- **Pattern**: Follows Tool pattern with decision frameworks\n- **Usability**: Clear protocol, report template, quick reference\n\n\n\nEvaluate this Skill against itself as a calibration exercise.\n",
  "encoding": "base64",

Identify the failing scenario\n2. Write test prompt for the scenario\n3. Run without skill — observe failure\n4. Document exact failure mode\n\n**GREEN Phase:**\n1. Write minimal skill addressing failure\n2. Run with skill — observe pass\n3. Verify failure mode resolved\n4. Document success criteria\n\n**REFACTOR Phase:**\n1. Remove duplication\n2. Tighten trigger accuracy\n3. Ensure reference depth compliance\n4. average — significant issues |\n| **F** | <60% (<72) | Poor — fundamental redesign needed |\n\n### Quality Thresholds\n\n| Score | Grade | Action |\n|-------|-------|--------|\n| 4.5+ | EXCELLENT | explain what Claude already knows (\"what is X\", \"how to write a for-loop\")\n- **NEVER** give high scores for well-formatted but redundant content\n- **NEVER** let length impress you — a 50-line Skill can outperform 500-line\n- **NEVER** forgive vague descriptions — poor description = skill never triggers\n- **NEVER** put \"when to use\" only in body — description is what Agent sees first\n- **NEVER** skip mentally testing decision trees\n\n## References\n\n- `references/01-skill-anatomy.md` — Full anatomy template\n- `references/02-frontmatter-standard.md` — YAML schema\n- `references/03-three-patterns.md` — Pattern system (HiveMind + Skill-Judge)\n- `references/04-tdd-workflow.md` — TDD methodology\n- `references/05-skill-quality-matrix.md` — Skill-Judge metrics (120-point system)\n- `references/06-knowledge-delta.md` — Expert vs Redundant vs Activation\n",
  "oldString": "---\nname: hivemind-skill-writer\ndescription: Use when creating, auditing, refactoring, or packaging HiveMind framework skills. Activates the meta-builder for skill authoring, TDD workflows, and quality validation. Bundles skill-writing guidance, Skill-Judge metrics, and HiveMind-specific packaging patterns.\nversion: 1.0.0\nframework: hivemind\npack: hivemind-skill-writer\nentry-level: L1\npattern: P1\nstacking: 0\nowner: hivemind\nstatus: active\n---\n\n# hivemind-skill-writer\n\n## Purpose\n\nMeta-builder skill for authoring HiveMind-specific skills. Use when you need to create, audit, refactor, or package skills for the HiveMind ecosystem.\n\n## When to Activate\n\n**Primary Triggers:**\n- User asks to create a new skill\n- User asks to audit existing skills\n- User asks to refactor skill structure\n- User asks to package skill sets\n- Intent involves skill authoring\n\n**Secondary Triggers:**\n- Detecting skill quality issues\n- Identifying skill redundancy\n- Planning skill migration\n\n## Core Philosophy\n\n### The Iron Law\n\n> **NO SKILL WITHOUT A FAILING TEST FIRST**\n\nEvery skill must be validated against a real failure scenario before being written.\n\n### Progressive Disclosure\n\n| Level | Content | When |\n|-------|---------|------|\n| **L1** | Metadata + overview | Always loaded (~100 words) |\n| **L2** | SKILL.md body | On trigger match (~500 lines) |\n| **L3** | Reference bundle | Explicit request |\n\n### The 3 Patterns\n\n**Pattern 1 — High-Level Routing**\n- Thin, must-load entry skills\n- Route to specialized sub-packs\n- Stacking: P1 + P2 or P1 + P3\n\n**Pattern 2 — Domain-Specific**\n- Deeper guidance for specific domains\n- Step-by-step with templates\n- Stacking: P2 standalone OR P1 + P2\n\n**Pattern 3 — Expertise Depth**\n- Vertical depth for complex scenarios\n- Activated when P1/P2 insufficient\n- Uses TOC + jump links\n\n## Skill Anatomy\n\nEvery HiveMind skill follows this structure:\n\n```\nskill-name/\n├── SKILL.md                    # Required entry\n├── references/                # L3 content\n│   ├── 01-topic-alpha.md     # Numbered for ordering\n│   ├── 02-topic-beta.md\n│   └── index.md              # TOC for P3\n├── scripts/                   # Discovery only\n│   └── detect-pattern.sh\n└── templates/                # Reusable\n    └── report-template.md\n```\n\n## Frontmatter Standard\n\n```yaml\n---\nname: skill-name-with-hyphens\ndescription: Use when [triggering conditions] — [effect] — [constraints]\nversion: 1.0.0\nframework: hivemind\npack: pack-name\nentry-level: L1|L2|L3\npattern: P1|P2|P3\nstacking: 0-3\nowner: hivemind\nstatus: active|deprecated|draft\n---\n```\n\n## TDD Workflow (RED-GREEN-REFACTOR)\n\n### RED Phase\n1. Identify the failing scenario\n2. Write test prompt for the scenario\n3. Run without skill — observe failure\n4. Document exact failure mode\n\n### GREEN Phase\n1. Write minimal skill addressing failure\n2. Run with skill — observe pass\n3. Verify failure mode resolved\n4. Document success criteria\n\n### REFACTOR Phase\n1. Remove duplication\n2. Tighten trigger accuracy\n3. Ensure reference depth compliance\n4. Validate stacking ≤3\n\n## Skill-Judge Quality Metrics\n\n| Dimension | Weight | Check |\n|-----------|--------|-------|\n| **Trigger Accuracy** | 25% | Description triggers on specific conditions |\n| **Action Coherence** | 25% | ONE thing well, no mission creep |\n| **Reference Integrity** | 20% | 1-level depth, no circular refs |\n| **Non-Redundancy** | 15% | No overlap with existing skills |\n| **Edge Case Coverage** | 15% | Handles degraded/delegated states |\n\n### Quality Thresholds\n\n| Score | Grade | Action |\n|-------|-------|--------|\n| 4.5+ | EXCELLENT | Ready for release |\n| 4.0+ | GOOD | Minor improvements |\n| 3.0+ | ACCEPTABLE | Address gaps |\n| <3.0 | NEEDS WORK | Major revision required |\n\n## Context-Intelligence Integration\n\nEvery skill must integrate with the context-intelligence pack:\n\n- **Entry State Recognition**: Acknowledge session state\n- **Trust Threshold**: Know minimum trust scores\n- **Rot Detection**: Watch for degradation signals\n- **Recovery Awareness**: Know when to escalate\n\n## Stacking Discipline\n\nAt entry, max **3 skills** may load:\n\n```\ncontext-intelligence (1) — always\ndelegation-scope (1) — if delegated\nworkflow-hierarchy (1) — if workflow\ncontext-rot-recovery (1) — if degraded\n```\n\n**hivemind-skill-writer does not count** against stack (stacking: 0).\n\n## References\n\n- `references/01-skill-anatomy.md` — Full anatomy template\n- `references/02-frontmatter-standard.md` — YAML schema\n- `references/03-three-patterns.md` — Pattern system details\n- `references/04-tdd-workflow.md` — TDD methodology\n- `references/05-skill-quality-matrix.md` — Skill-Judge metrics\n\n## Anti-Patterns\n\n**DO NOT:**\n- Create skills without failing test first\n- Use vague descriptions (\"Use when managing state\")\n- Exceed 1-level reference depth\n- Stack >3 skills at entry\n- Duplicate existing skill purposes\n- Force framework dogma over user intent\n\n**DO:**\n- Be specific in triggers (\"Use when delegation scope is ambiguous\")\n- Use progressive disclosure\n- Respect stacking limits\n- Integrate with context-intelligence\n- Follow the TDD workflow"

## Goal

Create a comprehensive skill revamp system for the HiveMind plugin, including:

## Discoveries

1. **GSD is legitimate, hive-* is pollution**: The project had it backwards — GSD (get-shit-done) framework is correct, hivemind governance skills were blocking direct action
2. **skill-judge has 120-point evaluation system** with 8 dimensions (D1-D8) focusing on Knowledge Delta as the core metric
3. **Knowledge Delta formula**: Good Skill = Expert-only Knowledge − What Claude Already Knows
4. **The 5 Patterns from skill-judge**: Mindset (~50 lines), Navigation (~30), Philosophy (~150), Process (~200), Tool (~300)
5. **Description is THE MOST IMPORTANT field** — determines if skill ever gets activated, must answer WHAT + WHEN + KEYWORDS
6. **Three types of knowledge**: Expert (keep), Activation (keep brief), Redundant (delete)
7. **Progressive disclosure is 3 layers**: L1 metadata (~100 tokens), L2 body (~500 lines), L3 references (on demand)
8. **Stacking discipline**: Max 3 skills at entry, hivemind-skill-writer has `stacking: 0` (meta skill)

Expert Knowledge (KEEP)\n- Domain-specific patterns not in general training\n- Proprietary workflows unique to the project\n- Institutional knowledge, conventions, decisions\n- **Action**: Preserve in references\n\n### 2. Instructions from: /Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/src/AGENTS.md
# src/ — Plugin Source Code

Source root for the OpenCode plugin. TypeScript, compiled to `dist/`.

## Boundary

Everything under `src/` ships as the npm package `hivemind-context-governance`.
The plugin entry is `plugin/opencode-plugin.ts` → registers hooks, tools, and event handlers.
Install/bootstrap authority lives in `cli/` + `control-plane/`; root markdown assets may describe that path but must not own it.
Stable governance and SOT paths should stay non-date-stamped. Compatibility aliases should point back to stable authority paths rather than become parallel authorities.

## Architecture

```
src/
├── plugin/          Assembly + enforcement wiring (NO business logic)
├── hooks/           Read-side/intercept — inject context and enforce in-band guards
├── tools/           Write-side — 6 structured agent-callable tools
├── sdk-supervisor/  Additive Phase 1 orchestration control (new sector)
├── schema-kernel/   Additive Phase 1 contract authority (new sector)
├── plugin-handlers/ Decision routing — command, tool, session resolution
├── core/            State — trajectory and workflow authority
├── commands/        Slash-command bundle registry, projection, and execution
├── context/         Prompt packet compilation and rendering
├── control-plane/   Gate/intake system for CLI commands
├── delegation/      Handoff packet creation and store
├── recovery/        State assessment, checkpoint, repair
├── governance/      Planning projection (minimal)
├── intelligence/    Doc surface routing + markdown-first read foundation
├── shared/          Utilities — paths, logging, runtime helpers
├── cli/             CLI entrypoint and command routing
└── cli.ts           CLI binary entrypoint
```

## SDK Usage Rules (Programmatic Governance)

The `src/` directory is strictly bound by the **Dual-Plane SDK Architecture**. Confusing these two API surfaces is the most fatal error in this codebase.

**1. The Control Plane (`@opencode-ai/sdk`)**
Code in `src/cli/` and `src/control-plane/` **MUST ONLY** import from `@opencode-ai/sdk`. This plane operates *outside* the agent loop. It is responsible for:
- Spawning local servers (`createOpencodeServer`)
- Initializing sessions (`client.session.create`)
- Managing high-level state.
*Never* use plugin hooks here.

**2. The Execution Plane (`@opencode-ai/plugin`)**
Code in `src/plugin/`, `src/hooks/`, and `src/tools/` **MUST ONLY** import from `@opencode-ai/plugin`. This plane operates *inside* the agent loop. It is responsible for:
- Registering custom native tools (`tool()`)
- Intercepting behavior (`system.transform`)
- Enforcing rules (`permission.ask`)
*Never* use the Client SDK here (it will cause infinite server recursion).

All code must use native SDK primitives:
- `tool.schema` (Zod) for tool argument validation inside plugins
- `permission.ask` interceptors instead of LLM system prompts for hard governance
- `tool.execute.after` to validate subagent returns (Zero-Trust Delegation)

## Verification Authority

- Behavioral claims about `src/` must prefer live OpenCode proof over local approximation.
- A real OpenCode server plus official client/plugin surfaces is the authoritative verification boundary for runtime determinism, session behavior, event flow, and hook behavior.
- Local bundle execution, direct tool instantiation, mock `PluginInput`, and ad hoc health fetches remain useful slice diagnostics, but they must not be presented as equivalent to live OpenCode verification.

## Phase 1 Direction

- `src/shared/` currently carries the live entry/runtime/turn contract seam.
- New durable contract ownership should move into `src/schema-kernel/` in additive slices instead of growing `src/shared/`.
- New orchestration behavior that coordinates sessions/workflows across turns should land in `src/sdk-supervisor/`, not in plugin hooks or oversized control-plane handlers.
- `src/tools/runtime/` is now the live reporting seam where schema-kernel runtime records and sdk-supervisor health summaries surface through `hivemind_runtime_status`; keep future reporting slices additive and inspection-first there instead of rebuilding ad hoc status logic elsewhere.

## Runtime Direction

- Prefer TS-owned feature behavior over markdown-only runtime logic.
- Keep root `commands/*.md` as thin OpenCode-facing projections; the source authority remains the registries and handlers under `src/`.
- Keep first-run and repair entry flows as the only writers of user-local `.opencode/**` runtime projection.
- Treat runtime diagnostics and live contract proof as separate evidence classes in tests, docs, and progress artifacts.

## Deprecated Modules (Audit 2026-03-15)

| Module | Issue | Action |
|--------|-------|--------|
| `core/session/` | Removed in L1 cutover; do not recreate | Keep session lifecycle in `hooks/start-work/` |
| `shared/event-bus.ts` | Removed in L1 cutover; do not recreate | Use SDK `event` hook |
| `hooks/soft-governance.ts` | Live toast-throttling helper | Keep using `client.tui.showToast()` |

</system-reminder>
```

```json
{
  "content": "---\nname: delegation-intelligence\ndescription: |\n  Decides WHEN to delegate vs. act directly, packages handoff context, validates scope inheritance.\n  \n  **Activation Triggers:**\n  - User asks to \"spawn\", \"delegate\", \"handoff\", \"fork\", \"run in parallel\"\n  - Task exceeds single-turn complexity\n  - Skill load exceeds capacity threshold\n  - Explicit /delegate command\n  \n  **What it does:**\n  - Routes to subagent OR acts directly based on complexity/effort\n  - Packages delegation packets with evidence requirements\n  - Enforces scope inheritance rules\n  - Validates zero-trust receipt confirmation\n  \n  **Keywords:** delegate, spawn, handoff, subagent, parallel, fork session\nversion: 1.0.0\ntags: [delegation, handoff, orchestration, gsd]\nstacking: 1\nentry: after-context-intelligence\nreferences:\n  - 01-delegation-routing.md\n  - 02-scope-inheritance.md\n  - 03-handoff-packet-format.md\n  - 04-zero-trust-validation.md\n  - index.md\n---\n\n# Delegation Intelligence\n\nDecides WHEN to delegate vs. act directly. Packages handoff context with evidence requirements. Enforces scope inheritance.\n\n## Philosophy\n\n**GSD Principle:** If you can do it in one turn, DO IT. Delegate only when:\n- Task requires parallel execution\n- Task will exceed complexity/effort threshold\n- Specialized skill required that agent lacks\n- User explicitly requests delegation\n\n**Delegation is NOT for:**\n- Avoiding work\n- Offloading thinking you should do yourself\n- Creating scope you can't track\n\n## Routing Decision Matrix\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                    COMPLEXITY ASSESSMENT                     │\n├─────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ LOW COMPLEXITY  │ ACT DIRECTLY                              │\n│ (< 30 min,      │ - Single tool or sequence                 │\n│  1-2 files,     │ - No specialized domain                   │\n│  no sub-tasks)  │ - Self-contained                          │\n├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ MED COMPLEXITY  │ DECOMPOSE + ACT                           │\n│ (30-60 min,     │ - Break into sequential steps             │\n│  3-5 files,     │ - Use GSD phases                         │\n│  some sub-tasks)│ - Track trajectory                        │\n├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│ HIGH COMPLEXITY │ DELEGATE                                  │\n│ (> 60 min,     │ - Spawn subagent with full packet         │\n│  5+ files,     │ - Set clear scope boundary                │\n│  many sub-tasks)│ - Define return contract                  │\n│  OR parallel    │ - Establish evidence requirements         │\n└─────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## Handoff Packet Requirements\n\nEvery delegation MUST include:\n\n### Required Fields\n```typescript\n{\n  sourceSession: string,      // Who is delegating\n  targetScope: string[],     // Exact files/features in scope\n  outOfScope: string[],      // Explicit boundary\n  evidence: {\n    required: string[],      // What must be delivered\n    format: string[],        // How evidence should be structured\n  },\n  returnContract: {\n    success: string,         // What \"done\" looks like\n    failure: string[],        // Failure conditions\n    escalationPath: string,   // Who to ask if stuck\n  },\n  trustLevel: 'full' | 'bounded' | 'minimal',\n}\n```\n\n### Trust Levels\n\n| Level | Permissions | Validation |\n|-------|-------------|------------|\n| **full** | Read/write/execute within scope | Light touch on return |\n| **bounded** | Read/write within scope, execute outside scope requires confirmation | Receipt + final validation |\n| **minimal** | Read-only, all actions require confirmation | Strict evidence review |\n\n## Scope Inheritance Rules\n\n**ALWAYS:**\n- Inherit project conventions and coding standards\n- Inherit relevant domain context from parent\n- Reference parent trajectory for prior decisions\n\n**NEVER:**\n- Expand scope beyond explicit boundary\n- Create new files outside stated scope\n- Modify shared infrastructure without approval\n- Assume parent has seen your intermediate work\n\n## Zero-Trust Receipt Validation\n\nOn subagent return:\n\n1. **Verify scope compliance** — Did they stay within bounds?\n2. **Check evidence quality** — Does it meet stated requirements?\n3. **Validate return contract** — Does success condition match reality?\n4. **Review trajectory** — Any suspicious deviations?\n\n**If validation FAILS:**\n- Log specific failure mode\n- Return to subagent with corrective feedback\n- Escalate to user if boundary violated\n\n## NEVER Do\n\n- Delegate without explicit scope boundary\n- Accept handoff without evidence requirements\n- Grant full trust on first delegation\n- Skip receipt validation\n- Expand scope without parent approval\n\n## Integration with context-intelligence\n\nDelegation-Intelligence runs AFTER context-intelligence assesses entry state:\n\n| Entry State | Delegation Behavior |\n|-------------|---------------------|\n| FRESH | Normal delegation routing |\n| RESUMED | Check subagent trajectory history before spawning |\n| DELEGATED | Return to parent before new delegation |\n| DEGRADED | Avoid delegation, act directly if possible |\n| POST-CANCEL | Verify clean handoff state before continuing |\n| LATE | Complete pending handoffs before new work |\n\n## See Also\n\n- `references/01-delegation-routing.md` — Decision routing details\n- `references/02-scope-inheritance.md` — Scope rules\n- `references/03-handoff-packet-format.md` — Packet structure\n- `references/04-zero-trust-validation.md` — Receipt validation\n",
  "filePath": "/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/skills/delegation-intelligence/SKILL.md"
}

  "content": "# Delegation Routing\n\nDecision tree for when to delegate vs. act directly.\n\n## Quick Routing Checklist\n\n```\n□ Can I complete this in one turn?        → ACT DIRECTLY\n□ Is parallelism beneficial?              → DELEGATE\n□ Do I need specialized capability?       → DELEGATE\n□ Is scope clearly bounded?                → DELEGATE (if yes to above)\n□ User explicitly requested delegation?    → DELEGATE\n□ I don't understand the domain?          → DELEGATE\n□ Task is exploratory/research?            → ACT DIRECTLY (until scope known)\n```\n\n## Complexity Scoring\n\n| Score | Time | Files | Sub-tasks | Decision |\n|-------|------|-------|-----------|----------|\n| 1 | < 15 min | 1 | 0 | Act |\n| 2 | 15-30 min | 1-2 | 0-1 | Act |\n| 3 | 30-60 min | 2-3 | 2-3 | Decompose |\n| 4 | 60-120 min | 3-5 | 4-6 | Delegate |\n| 5 | > 120 min | 5+ | 6+ | Delegate |\n\n## Delegation Triggers\n\n### Explicit Triggers (Delegate immediately)\n- User says: \"spawn\", \"delegate\", \"run in parallel\", \"fork\"\n- Task clearly needs multiple simultaneous workers\n- Specialized skill required (e.g., \"fix the DB schema\")\n\n### Implicit Triggers (Assess complexity first)\n- Task spans > 3 files\n- Requires cross-cutting changes\n- Has unknown unknowns\n- Multi-phase implementation\n\n### Anti-Triggers (Do NOT delegate)\n- \"Just quickly check...\" — almost always act\n- Exploratory questions — act until scope known\n- Trivial edits — act\n- User asking for your opinion — act\n\n## Routing Examples\n\n### Example 1: Quick Fix\n```\nUser: \"Fix the typo in README\"\n→ Score: 1 → ACT DIRECTLY\n```\n\n### Example 2: Feature Implementation\n```\nUser: \"Add user authentication\"\n→ Score: 4-5 → DELEGATE\n→ Package: Full handoff packet with scope\n```\n\n### Example 3: Research Task\n```\nUser: \"What's the architecture of subsystem X?\"\n→ Score: 2-3 → ACT DIRECTLY\n→ Scope may expand — stay in control\n```\n\n## Parallel Execution Rules\n\nWhen delegating for parallel execution:\n\n1. **Divide scope mutually exclusive** — No overlapping files\n2. **Set explicit boundaries** — What each worker owns\n3. **Define merge strategy** — Who resolves conflicts\n4. **Establish communication** — How to share intermediate findings\n",

├── Coding standards\n│   ├── Naming conventions\n│   ├── Tech stack knowledge\n│   └── Architecture understanding\n├── Trajectory History       ✅ INHERITED (reference)\n│   ├── Prior decisions\n│   ├── Rejected approaches\n│   └── User preferences\n├── Explicit Scope           ✅ GRANTED\n│   ├── Assigned files\n│   ├── Assigned features\n│   └── Evidence requirements\n└── Implicit Permissions     ❌ NOT INHERITED\n    ├── Unstated file access\n    ├── Infrastructure changes\n    └── New file creation (unless scoped)\n```\n\n## Scope Boundaries\n\n### Hard Boundaries (NEVER cross without approval)\n- `src/shared/` — Shared utilities\n- `src/plugin/` — Plugin core\n- `.opencode/` — Agent configuration\n- `AGENTS.md` — Governance files\n- Any file explicitly marked out-of-scope\n\n### Soft Boundaries (Caution advised)\n- `src/core/` — Core state management\n- `src/hooks/` — Hook implementations\n- Any file that appears in multiple feature scopes\n\n### Green Light (Can modify within scope)\n- Files explicitly assigned\n- Test files for assigned features\n- Documentation for assigned features\n\n## Inheritance Rules Summary\n\n| Context Type | Inheritance |\n|-------------|-------------|\n| Coding standards | Always inherit |\n| Naming conventions | Always inherit |\n| Prior decisions | Reference but verify |\n| User preferences | Verify they still apply |\n| Out-of-scope items | NEVER touch |\n| Shared utilities | Ask first |\n| New files | Only if scoped |\n\n## Scope Expansion Protocol\n\nIf subagent discovers scope needs expansion:\n\n1. **STOP** — Do not proceed beyond boundary\n2. **Document** — What is needed and why\n3. **Return** — To parent with evidence\n4. **Wait** — For explicit approval or revised scope\n5. **Resume** — Only after approved scope update\n\n## Anti-Patterns\n\n### ❌ \"I'll just quickly fix X while I'm here\"\nScope creep. Unless X is in scope, don't touch it.\n\n### ❌ \"The parent probably knows about this\"\nVerify. Don't assume inheritance of decisions.\n\n### ❌ \"I need to update shared/ to make this work\"\nEscalate. Shared utilities require parent approval.\n\n### ❌ \"This is obviously the right approach\"\nDocument the reasoning for parent review.\n",

{
  "content": "# Handoff Packet Format\n\nStructure for delegation context packages.\n\n## Packet Schema\n\n```typescript\ninterface DelegationPacket {\n  // Identity\n  packetId: string,           // Unique ID: delegator-timestamp-sequence\n  sourceSession: string,       // Parent session ID\n  targetAgent: string,         // Agent type to spawn\n  createdAt: string,           // ISO timestamp\n  \n  // Scope Definition\n  scope: {\n    inScope: string[],         // Files/features in scope\n    outOfScope: string[],      // Explicit exclusions\n    boundaryReason: string,   // Why scope is bounded this way\n  },\n  \n  // Task Definition\n  task: {\n    description: string,       // What to accomplish\n    successCriteria: string[], // Done conditions\n    priority: 'critical' | 'high' | 'medium' | 'low',\n    deadline?: string,         // Optional deadline\n  },\n  \n  // Evidence Requirements\n  evidence: {\n    required: string[],        // What must be delivered\n    intermediate?: string[],   // Optional checkpoints\n    format: string[],           // How to structure evidence\n    minimumQuality: string,    // Quality threshold\n  },\n  \n  // Return Contract\n  returnContract: {\n    successCondition: string,  // What \"done\" looks like\n    failureModes: string[],     // Known failure risks\n    escalationPath: string,    // Who/how to escalate\n    rollbackPlan?: string,     // How to undo if needed\n  },\n  \n  // Trust Configuration\n  trust: {\n    level: 'full' | 'bounded' | 'minimal',\n    permissions: string[],     // Explicit permissions\n    restrictions: string[],     // Explicit restrictions\n    reviewRequired: string[],   // Actions needing parent review\n  },\n  \n  // Context Inheritance\n  inheritedContext: {\n    conventions: string[],     // Coding standards to follow\n    priorDecisions: string[],   // Relevant trajectory items\n    userPreferences: string[],  // Known user preferences\n    blockedApproaches: string[],// Previously rejected methods\n  },\n  \n  // Metadata\n  metadata: {\n    parentTrajectory: string,   // Link to parent trajectory\n    delegationReason: string,   // Why delegation was chosen\n    parallelTasks?: string[],   // Other parallel delegations\n    mergeStrategy?: string,     // How to combine results\n  }\n}\n```\n\n## Minimal Packet (Bounded Trust)\n\nFor bounded trust delegations, minimum required:\n\n```typescript\n{\n  sourceSession: string,\n  scope: { inScope: string[], outOfScope: string[] },\n  task: { description: string, successCriteria: string[] },\n  evidence: { required: string[] },\n  returnContract: { successCondition: string },\n  trust: { level: 'bounded' }\n}\n```\n\n## Quality Checklist\n\nBefore sending packet, verify:\n\n- [ ] Scope is explicit, not implied\n- [ ] Success criteria are measurable\n- [ ] Evidence requirements are clear\n- [ ] Trust level matches task risk\n- [ ] Parent trajectory is referenced\n- [ ] Escalation path is defined\n\n## Packet Creation Flow\n\n1. **Assess** — Complexity, parallelism needs\n2. **Scope** — Define explicit boundaries\n3. **Package** — Fill required fields\n4. **Validate** — Checklist verification\n5. **Send** — Via `hivemind_handoff` tool\n6. **Track** — Monitor for receipt confirmation\n",

  "content": "# Zero-Trust Validation\n\nReceipt validation for delegated tasks.\n\n## Core Principle\n\n**Never trust, always verify.** Delegation receipt requires validation before accepting results.\n\n## Validation Pipeline\n\n```\nSUBAGENT RETURNS\n      │\n      ▼\n┌─────────────────┐\n│ 1. RECEIPT      │ → Acknowledge receipt, start validation\n│    CHECK        │\n└────────┬────────┘\n         │\n         ▼\n┌─────────────────┐\n│ 2. SCOPE        │ → Did they stay within bounds?\n│    COMPLIANCE   │\n└────────┬────────┘\n         │\n    ┌────┴────┐\n    │ PASS?   │\n    └────┬────┘\n         │ NO\n         ▼\n    ┌─────────────────┐\n    │ ESCALATE        │ → Log violation, return to subagent\n    │ TO PARENT       │\n    └─────────────────┘\n         │\n        YES\n         ▼\n┌─────────────────┐\n│ 3. EVIDENCE     │ → Does evidence meet requirements?\n│    QUALITY      │\n└────────┬────────┘\n         │\n    ┌────┴────┐\n    │ PASS?   │\n    └────┬────┘\n         │ NO\n         ▼\n    ┌─────────────────┐\n    │ RETURN          │ → Send back for correction\n    │ FOR REMEDIATION │\n    └─────────────────┘\n         │\n        YES\n         ▼\n┌─────────────────┐\n│ 4. RETURN       │ → Validate success condition\n│    CONTRACT     │\n└────────┬────────┘\n         │\n    ┌────┴────┐\n    │ PASS?   │\n    └────┬────┘\n         │ NO\n         ▼\n    ┌─────────────────┐\n    │ DISPUTE         │ → Document disagreement\n    │ RESOLUTION      │ → Escalate if needed\n    └─────────────────┘\n         │\n        YES\n         ▼\n┌─────────────────┐\n│ 5. ACCEPT       │ → Merge results, close delegation\n│    & MERGE      │\n└─────────────────┘\n```\n\n## Scope Compliance Check\n\n| Check | Question |\n|-------|----------|\n| File access | Did they only touch in-scope files? |\n| New files | Were new files within scope? |\n| Modifications | Did changes stay within scope? |\n| Shared code | Did they avoid modifying shared utilities? |\n\n### If Scope Violated\n\n```typescript\n{\n  violation: {\n    type: 'out_of_scope_access',\n    file: string,\n    action: 'read' | 'write' | 'delete',\n    severity: 'minor' | 'major' | 'critical',\n  },\n  response: 'remediate' | 'escalate' | 'reject',\n  remediation: string, // What subagent must do\n}\n```\n\n## Evidence Quality Check\n\n| Quality | Criteria |\n|---------|----------|\n| **Acceptable** | Meets all required evidence, minimum quality threshold |\n| **Incomplete** | Missing some required evidence |\n| **Substandard** | Evidence present but below quality threshold |\n| **Falsified** | Evidence doesn't match actual work |\n\n### Quality Dimensions\n\n1. **Completeness** — All required evidence present\n2. **Accuracy** — Evidence matches actual changes\n3. **Traceability** — Clear link to original requirements\n4. **Format** — Follows specified structure\n\n## Return Contract Validation\n\n### Success Condition Check\n\n\"Is the success condition actually met?\"\n\n1. Parse success condition into measurable criteria\n2. Check each criterion against evidence\n3. Document any gaps\n4. Accept only if ALL criteria met\n\n### Failure Mode Review\n\n\"Did any known failure modes occur?\"\n\n- Document any occurred failure modes\n- Assess impact on overall success\n- Determine if remediation possible\n- Decide: accept with caveats OR reject\n\n## Escalation Triggers\n\nEscalate to parent (or user) if:\n\n- Scope violated in major way\n- Evidence appears falsified\n- Success condition disputed and can't resolve\n- Subagent unresponsive after remediation\n- Trust level violated\n\n## Validation Tools\n\nUse `hivemind_handoff` tool for:\n- Receipt confirmation\n- Evidence submission\n- Validation disputes\n- Delegation closure\n",
  "filePath": "/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/skills/delegation-intelligence/references/04-zero-trust-validation.md"
}

## Assistant (Build · MiniMax-M2.7 · 31.3s)

_Thinking:_

Now let me create the Workflow-Coordination SKILL.md.

**Tool: write**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "content": "---\nname: workflow-coordination\ndescription: |\n  Orchestrates multi-phase workflows, manages phase transitions, validates milestone completion.\n  \n  **Activation Triggers:**\n  - User says \"execute plan\", \"run workflow\", \"complete phase\"\n  - Task requires multi-phase approach (research → plan → execute → verify)\n  - Milestone completion needs validation\n  - Phase transition requires gate check\n  \n  **What it does:**\n  - Routes task to appropriate phase workflow\n  - Manages phase dependencies and transitions\n  - Validates completion gates\n  - Coordinates parallel vs. sequential execution\n  \n  **Keywords:** workflow, phase, milestone, execute, transition, gate, validate\nversion: 1.0.0\ntags: [workflow, orchestration, phases, milestones, gsd]\nstacking: 1\nentry: after-context-intelligence\nreferences:\n  - 01-phase-lifecycle.md\n  - 02-transition-gates.md\n  - 03-milestone-tracking.md\n  - 04-parallel-coordination.md\n  - index.md\n---\n\n# Workflow Coordination\n\nOrchestrates multi-phase workflows from initiation through completion. Manages phase transitions with validation gates. Coordinates parallel execution when beneficial.\n\n## Philosophy\n\n**GSD Principle:** Every workflow has phases. Skip phases at your own risk.\n\n**Phase Workflows are NOT optional** for:\n- New features with > 3 tasks\n- Multi-file refactors\n- Any task spanning > 1 hour\n- Any task requiring testing\n\n**Phase Workflows can be LIGHTWEIGHT for:**\n- Quick fixes (< 15 min)\n- Single file changes\n- Documentation updates\n- Research tasks\n\n## Standard Phase Sequence\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│                    TYPICAL WORKFLOW                          │\n├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n│                                                              │\n│  DISCOVER   →   PLAN   →   EXECUTE   →   VERIFY   →  COMPLETE│\n│    │            │           │             │               │\n│    │            │           │             │               │\n│    ▼            ▼           ▼             ▼               │\n│ Context    Decompose   Implement     Validate          Document│\n│ Assess     Tasks       Changes       Results         & Close │\n│                                                              │\n└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\n## Phase Definitions\n\n### DISCOVER Phase\n**Purpose:** Understand task scope, constraints, and context\n\n**Activities:**\n- Analyze user requirements\n- Identify dependencies\n- Assess complexity\n- Map existing infrastructure\n- Identify risks\n\n**Exit Gate:** Clear problem statement with scope boundary\n\n### PLAN Phase\n**Purpose:** Decompose into executable steps\n\n**Activities:**\n- Break into sequential/parallel tasks\n- Estimate effort\n- Define dependencies\n- Set milestones\n- Define success criteria\n\n**Exit Gate:** Approved plan with measurable outcomes\n\n### EXECUTE Phase\n**Purpose:** Implement changes\n\n**Activities:**\n- Make code changes\n- Run tests\n- Update documentation\n- Seek clarification if needed\n\n**Exit Gate:** All changes made, tests passing\n\n### VERIFY Phase\n**Purpose:** Validate results against requirements\n\n**Activities:**\n- Run full test suite\n- Verify against success criteria\n- Check for regressions\n- Validate user acceptance\n\n**Exit Gate:** Confirmed by evidence\n\n### COMPLETE Phase\n**Purpose:** Clean close and documentation\n\n**Activities:**\n- Document decisions\n- Clean up artifacts\n- Close milestone\n- Summarize results\n\n## Transition Gates\n\nEvery phase transition requires gate validation:\n\n```\nDISCOVER → PLAN: \"Is scope clear? Are constraints known?\"\nPLAN → EXECUTE: \"Is plan approved? Are dependencies resolved?\"\nEXECUTE → VERIFY: \"Are changes complete? Is evidence ready?\"\nVERIFY → COMPLETE: \"Do results meet criteria? Is user satisfied?\"\n```\n\n### Gate Validation Checklist\n\n| Gate | Question | Evidence Required |\n|------|----------|-------------------|\n| Discover→Plan | Scope clear? | Problem statement |\n| Plan→Execute | Plan approved? | Task list, estimates |\n| Execute→Verify | Changes done? | Code diff, test results |\n| Verify→Complete | Criteria met? | Validation report |\n\n## FAIL Gates\n\n**STOP IMMEDIATELY if:**\n- Evidence of harm (data loss, security issue)\n- Fundamental scope change\n- Resource exhaustion\n- User requests stop\n\n## Milestone Tracking\n\n### Milestone Structure\n\n```typescript\ninterface Milestone {\n  id: string,\n  name: string,\n  phases: Phase[],\n  status: 'pending' | 'active' | 'complete' | 'blocked',\n  startedAt?: string,\n  completedAt?: string,\n  blockers?: string[],\n}\n```\n\n### Milestone States\n\n```\nPENDING → ACTIVE → COMPLETE\n              ↓\n           BLOCKED → (resolved) → ACTIVE\n```\n\n## Parallel Coordination\n\nWhen EXECUTE phase benefits from parallelism:\n\n### Parallel Patterns\n\n**Pattern 1: Embarrassingly Parallel**\n```\nTask A → independent → Result A\nTask B → independent → Result B\nTask C → independent → Result C\n         ↓\n    MERGE Results\n```\n\n**Pattern 2: Pipeline Parallel**\n```\nPhase 1: A → B → C (sequential within phase)\n                  ↓\nPhase 2: D → E → F (can start when C done)\n```\n\n**Pattern 3: Fan-out/Fan-in**\n```\n        → Task B →\nTask A →          → MERGE\n        → Task C →\n```\n\n### Coordination Rules\n\n1. **Scope division** — Tasks must be independent\n2. **Merge strategy** — Who resolves conflicts\n3. **Communication** — How to share intermediate state\n4. **Failure handling** — What happens if one fails\n\n## NEVER Do\n\n- Skip DISCOVER for complex tasks\n- Skip VERIFY before COMPLETE\n- Merge parallel results without conflict resolution\n- Close milestone without user sign-off\n- Skip gate validation to \"save time\"\n\n## Integration with context-intelligence\n\nWorkflow-Coordination runs AFTER context-intelligence:\n\n| Entry State | Workflow Behavior |\n|-------------|-------------------|\n| FRESH | Normal workflow initiation |\n| RESUMED | Resume from last incomplete phase |\n| DELEGATED | Check delegation status before new workflow |\n| DEGRADED | Use minimal workflow, heavy validation |\n| POST-CANCEL | Clean close of canceled workflow |\n| LATE | Prioritize verification over exploration |\n\n## See Also\n\n- `references/01-phase-lifecycle.md` — Phase details\n- `references/02-transition-gates.md` — Gate validation\n- `references/03-milestone-tracking.md` — Milestone management\n- `references/04-parallel-coordination.md` — Parallel execution\n",
  "filePath": "/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/skills/workflow-coordination/SKILL.md"
}
```

**Output:**
```
Wrote file successfully.
```

Now let me create all 4 reference files for Workflow-Coordination.

**Tool: write**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "content": "# Phase Lifecycle\n\nDetailed phase definitions and activities.\n\n## DISCOVER Phase\n\n**Goal:** Understand the problem space\n\n### Activities\n\n1. **Requirement Analysis**\n   - What is the user asking for?\n   - What problem does it solve?\n   - Who benefits?\n\n2. **Scope Assessment**\n   - What's in scope?\n   - What's explicitly out of scope?\n   - What might be tempting but shouldn't be?\n\n3. **Context Gathering**\n   - Existing code affected?\n   - Dependencies?\n   - Constraints (time, tech stack, permissions)?\n\n4. **Risk Identification**\n   - Technical risks\n   - Scope risks\n   - Resource risks\n\n### Exit Criteria\n\n- [ ] Problem statement written\n- [ ] Scope boundary defined\n- [ ] Key constraints identified\n- [ ] Initial risk list created\n\n### Exit Evidence\n\n```\nPROBLEM: [1-2 sentence problem statement]\nSCOPE: [in scope items], [out of scope items]\nCONSTRAINTS: [known constraints]\nRISKS: [top 3 risks]\n```\n\n## PLAN Phase\n\n**Goal:** Create executable roadmap\n\n### Activities\n\n1. **Task Decomposition**\n   - Break into 1-5 day work units\n   - Identify dependencies\n   - Order logically\n\n2. **Effort Estimation**\n   - Estimate each task\n   - Total timeline\n   - Milestone points\n\n3. **Dependency Mapping**\n   - What must come first\n   - What can be parallel\n   - What has external dependencies\n\n4. **Success Criteria Definition**\n   - How do we know each task is done?\n   - How do we know the whole thing is done?\n   - What does success look like?\n\n### Exit Criteria\n\n- [ ] Task list with estimates\n- [ ] Milestone definitions\n- [ ] Dependency graph\n- [ ] Success criteria documented\n\n### Exit Evidence\n\n```\nTASKS:\n1. [Task] - [Estimate] - [Dependency]\n2. [Task] - [Estimate] - [Dependency]\n...\n\nMILESTONES:\nM1: [Date] - [Tasks included]\nM2: [Date] - [Tasks included]\n\nSUCCESS CRITERIA:\n1. [Criterion]\n2. [Criterion]\n```\n\n## EXECUTE Phase\n\n**Goal:** Implement changes\n\n### Activities\n\n1. **Implementation**\n   - Write code\n   - Follow project conventions\n   - Keep changes focused\n\n2. **Testing**\n   - Unit tests\n   - Integration tests\n   - Manual verification\n\n3. **Documentation**\n   - Code comments\n   - README updates\n   - API docs\n\n4. **Iterative Refinement**\n   - Refactor as needed\n   - Address tech debt\n   - Seek clarification\n\n### Exit Criteria\n\n- [ ] All planned changes implemented\n- [ ] Tests passing\n- [ ] Documentation updated\n- [ ] No known regressions\n\n### Exit Evidence\n\n```\nCHANGES:\n- [file]: [change summary]\n...\n\nTESTS:\n- [test suite]: [result]\n- [integration test]: [result]\n\nDOCS:\n- [updated files]\n```\n\n## VERIFY Phase\n\n**Goal:** Confirm results meet requirements\n\n### Activities\n\n1. **Test Suite Run**\n   - Full unit test suite\n   - Integration tests\n   - E2E tests if applicable\n\n2. **Success Criteria Check**\n   - Go through each criterion\n   - Document pass/fail\n   - Note any gaps\n\n3. **Regression Check**\n   - What could have broken?\n   - Verify nothing did\n\n4. **User Acceptance**\n   - Demo if applicable\n   - Get user sign-off\n\n### Exit Criteria\n\n- [ ] All success criteria met\n- [ ] No regressions\n- [ ] User acceptance obtained\n\n### Exit Evidence\n\n```\nVERIFICATION:\n✓ [criterion 1]\n✓ [criterion 2]\n⚠ [criterion 3] - [note]\n\nREGRESSION: [none detected / issues found]\nUSER SIGN-OFF: [yes / no / pending]\n```\n\n## COMPLETE Phase\n\n**Goal:** Clean close\n\n### Activities\n\n1. **Artifact Cleanup**\n   - Remove temporary files\n   - Archive working files\n   - Clean up test artifacts\n\n2. **Decision Documentation**\n   - Record key decisions\n   - Document rejected alternatives\n   - Note lessons learned\n\n3. **Milestone Close**\n   - Update tracking\n   - Close issues\n   - Notify stakeholders\n\n4. **Handoff**\n   - Summarize results\n   - Provide run instructions\n   - Set up for maintenance\n\n### Exit Criteria\n\n- [ ] All artifacts cleaned\n- [ ] Decisions documented\n- [ ] Milestone closed\n- [ ] User satisfied\n\n### Exit Evidence\n\n```\nMILESTONE CLOSED: [date]\nSUMMARY: [1 paragraph what was accomplished]\nARTIFACTS: [list of final deliverables]\nMAINTAINABILITY: [how to maintain / extend]\n```\n",
  "filePath": "/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/skills/workflow-coordination/references/01-phase-lifecycle.md"
}

  "content": "# Transition Gates\n\nValidation points between phases.\n\n## Gate Philosophy\n\n**Gates are CHECKPOINTS, not OBSTACLES.**\n\nGood gates:\n- Catch problems early\n- Provide evidence of progress\n- Enable course correction\n- Protect downstream phases\n\nBad gates:\n- Block without reason\n- Require excessive documentation\n- Don't add value\n\n## Gate Types\n\n### Soft Gates\n- Used for internal workflow\n- Can be self-validated\n- Enable fast iteration\n\n### Hard Gates\n- Used for phase transitions\n- Require explicit evidence\n- Block until passed\n\n## Gate Validation\n\n### DISCOVER → PLAN Gate\n\n**Question:** \"Is scope clear enough to plan?\"\n\n| Check | Question | Evidence |\n|-------|----------|----------|\n| Scope | Is boundary defined? | Written scope statement |\n| Context | Is context sufficient? | Relevant files identified |\n| Risks | Are major risks known? | Risk list with mitigations |\n\n**Pass:** Scope document exists, constraints known\n**Fail:** Scope fuzzy, major unknowns remain\n\n### PLAN → EXECUTE Gate\n\n**Question:** \"Is plan approved and ready?\"\n\n| Check | Question | Evidence |\n|-------|----------|----------|\n| Tasks | Are tasks clear? | Numbered task list |\n| Estimates | Are estimates realistic? | Time estimates per task |\n| Dependencies | Are dependencies resolved? | Dependency graph |\n| Criteria | Are success criteria defined? | Measurable outcomes |\n\n**Pass:** Plan approved (user or self for internal)\n**Fail:** Tasks unclear, major dependencies unresolved\n\n### EXECUTE → VERIFY Gate\n\n**Question:** \"Are changes complete?\"\n\n| Check | Question | Evidence |\n|-------|----------|----------|\n| Implementation | Is code complete? | Diff of all changes |\n| Tests | Are tests passing? | Test output |\n| Coverage | Is coverage adequate? | Coverage report |\n| Docs | Are docs updated? | Updated files listed |\n\n**Pass:** All planned changes, tests green\n**Fail:** Incomplete implementation, failing tests\n\n### VERIFY → COMPLETE Gate\n\n**Question:** \"Do results meet criteria?\"\n\n| Check | Question | Evidence |\n|-------|----------|----------|\n| Criteria | All criteria met? | Verification checklist |\n| Quality | Is quality acceptable? | Quality assessment |\n| User | Is user satisfied? | User sign-off |\n\n**Pass:** All criteria green, user satisfied\n**Fail:** Criteria unmet, user concerns remain\n\n## FAIL Gates\n\n### Critical Fail Conditions\n\nThese gates STOP work immediately:\n\n```\n🚫 EVIDENCE OF HARM\n   - Data corruption\n   - Security vulnerability\n   - Data loss\n\n🚫 SCOPE CREEP\n   - User requests significantly different goal\n   - New requirements that invalidate plan\n\n🚫 RESOURCE EXHAUSTION\n   - Time limit reached\n   - Budget exhausted\n   - External dependency unavailable\n\n🚫 USER CANCEL\n   - User explicitly requests stop\n```\n\n### FAIL Gate Protocol\n\n1. **STOP** — Don't continue\n2. **DOCUMENT** — Record what happened\n3. **ESCALATE** — Inform user\n4. **PROPOSE** — Path forward (continue / abort / revise)\n\n## Gate Documentation\n\n```typescript\ninterface GateRecord {\n  gateId: string,\n  fromPhase: Phase,\n  toPhase: Phase,\n  status: 'passed' | 'failed' | 'bypassed',\n  evidence: {\n    provided: string[],\n    required: string[],\n  },\n  validationMethod: 'self' | 'peer' | 'user',\n  validatedBy?: string,\n  validatedAt: string,\n  notes?: string,\n}\n```\n\n## Gate Examples\n\n### Example 1: Passing DISCOVER→PLAN\n\n```\nSCOPE: User wants password reset feature\nCONSTRAINTS: Must use existing auth system\nRISKS: Email delivery reliability\n\n→ Scope clear, context sufficient, risks identified\n→ PASS\n```\n\n### Example 2: Failing PLAN→EXECUTE\n\n```\nTASKS:\n1. Add reset endpoint\n2. Add email service\n3. Add UI flow\n\nDEPENDENCIES:\n- Email service needs API key (not yet available)\n\n→ Task list clear, but dependency unresolved\n→ FAIL (must get API key first)\n```\n\n### Example 3: FAIL Gate\n\n```\nUser: \"Actually, I wanted passwordLESS auth, not reset\"\n\n→ Fundamental scope change\n→ FAIL GATE\n→ Document current state\n→ Propose: Close current, start new discovery\n```\n",

}
