<content>1: ---
2: name: delegation-intelligence
3: description: |
4:   Decides WHEN to delegate vs. act directly, packages handoff context, validates scope inheritance.
5:   
6:   **Activation Triggers:**
7:   - User asks to "spawn", "delegate", "handoff", "fork", "run in parallel"
8:   - Task exceeds single-turn complexity
9:   - Skill load exceeds capacity threshold
10:   - Explicit /delegate command
11:   
12:   **What it does:**
13:   - Routes to subagent OR acts directly based on complexity/effort
14:   - Packages delegation packets with evidence requirements
15:   - Enforces scope inheritance rules
16:   - Validates zero-trust receipt confirmation
17:   
18:   **Keywords:** delegate, spawn, handoff, subagent, parallel, fork session
19: version: 1.0.0
20: tags: [delegation, handoff, orchestration, gsd]
21: stacking: 1
22: entry: after-context-intelligence
23: references:
24:   - 01-delegation-routing.md
25:   - 02-scope-inheritance.md
26:   - 03-handoff-packet-format.md
27:   - 04-zero-trust-validation.md
28:   - index.md
29: ---
30: 
31: # Delegation Intelligence
32: 
33: Decides WHEN to delegate vs. act directly. Packages handoff context with evidence requirements. Enforces scope inheritance.
34: 
35: ## Philosophy
36: 
37: **GSD Principle:** If you can do it in one turn, DO IT. Delegate only when:
38: - Task requires parallel execution
39: - Task will exceed complexity/effort threshold
40: - Specialized skill required that agent lacks
41: - User explicitly requests delegation
42: 
43: **Delegation is NOT for:**
44: - Avoiding work
45: - Offloading thinking you should do yourself
46: - Creating scope you can't track
47: 
48: ## Routing Decision Matrix
49: 
50: ```
51: ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
52: │                    COMPLEXITY ASSESSMENT                     │
53: ├─────────────────┬───────────────────────────────────────────┤
54: │ LOW COMPLEXITY  │ ACT DIRECTLY                              │
55: │ (< 30 min,      │ - Single tool or sequence                 │
56: │  1-2 files,     │ - No specialized domain                   │
57: │  no sub-tasks)  │ - Self-contained                          │
58: ├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤
59: │ MED COMPLEXITY  │ DECOMPOSE + ACT                           │
60: │ (30-60 min,     │ - Break into sequential steps             │
61: │  3-5 files,     │ - Use GSD phases                         │
62: │  some sub-tasks)│ - Track trajectory                        │
63: ├─────────────────┼───────────────────────────────────────────┤
64: │ HIGH COMPLEXITY │ DELEGATE                                  │
65: │ (> 60 min,     │ - Spawn subagent with full packet         │
66: │  5+ files,     │ - Set clear scope boundary                │
67: │  many sub-tasks)│ - Define return contract                  │
68: │  OR parallel    │ - Establish evidence requirements         │
69: └─────────────────┴───────────────────────────────────────────┘
70: ```
71: 
72: ## Handoff Packet Requirements
73: 
74: Every delegation MUST include:
75: 
76: ### Required Fields
77: ```typescript
78: {
79:   sourceSession: string,      // Who is delegating
80:   targetScope: string[],     // Exact files/features in scope
81:   outOfScope: string[],      // Explicit boundary
82:   evidence: {
83:     required: string[],      // What must be delivered
84:     format: string[],        // How evidence should be structured
85:   },
86:   returnContract: {
87:     success: string,         // What "done" looks like
88:     failure: string[],        // Failure conditions
89:     escalationPath: string,   // Who to ask if stuck
90:   },
91:   trustLevel: 'full' | 'bounded' | 'minimal',
92: }
93: ```
94: 
95: ### Trust Levels
96: 
97: | Level | Permissions | Validation |
98: |-------|-------------|------------|
99: | **full** | Read/write/execute within scope | Light touch on return |
100: | **bounded** | Read/write within scope, execute outside scope requires confirmation | Receipt + final validation |
101: | **minimal** | Read-only, all actions require confirmation | Strict evidence review |
102: 
103: ## Scope Inheritance Rules
104: 
105: **ALWAYS:**
106: - Inherit project conventions and coding standards
107: - Inherit relevant domain context from parent
108: - Reference parent trajectory for prior decisions
109: 
110: **NEVER:**
111: - Expand scope beyond explicit boundary
112: - Create new files outside stated scope
113: - Modify shared infrastructure without approval
114: - Assume parent has seen your intermediate work
115: 
116: ## Zero-Trust Receipt Validation
117: 
118: On subagent return:
119: 
120: 1. **Verify scope compliance** — Did they stay within bounds?
121: 2. **Check evidence quality** — Does it meet stated requirements?
122: 3. **Validate return contract** — Does success condition match reality?
123: 4. **Review trajectory** — Any suspicious deviations?
124: 
125: **If validation FAILS:**
126: - Log specific failure mode
127: - Return to subagent with corrective feedback
128: - Escalate to user if boundary violated
129: 
130: ## NEVER Do
131: 
132: - Delegate without explicit scope boundary
133: - Accept handoff without evidence requirements
134: - Grant full trust on first delegation
135: - Skip receipt validation
136: - Expand scope without parent approval
137: 
138: ## Integration with context-intelligence
139: 
140: Delegation-Intelligence runs AFTER context-intelligence assesses entry state:
141: 
142: | Entry State | Delegation Behavior |
143: |-------------|---------------------|
144: | FRESH | Normal delegation routing |
145: | RESUMED | Check subagent trajectory history before spawning |
146: | DELEGATED | Return to parent before new delegation |
147: | DEGRADED | Avoid delegation, act directly if possible |
148: | POST-CANCEL | Verify clean handoff state before continuing |
149: | LATE | Complete pending handoffs before new work |
150: 
151: ## See Also
152: 
153: - `references/01-delegation-routing.md` — Decision routing details
154: - `references/02-scope-inheritance.md` — Scope rules
155: - `references/03-handoff-packet-format.md` — Packet structure
156: - `references/04-zero-trust-validation.md` — Receipt validation

(End of file - total 156 lines)
</content>

14: 
15: # hivemind-skill-writer
16: 
17: ## Purpose
18: 
19: Meta-builder skill for authoring HiveMind-specific skills. Use when creating, auditing, refactoring, or packaging skills for the HiveMind ecosystem.
20: 
21: ## When to Activate
22: 
23: **Primary Triggers (answer WHAT + WHEN + KEYWORDS):**
24: - "create a new skill"
25: - "write a skill for..."
26: - "audit this skill"
27: - "is this skill good"
28: - "skill quality check"
29: - "skill design"
30: - "skill authoring"
31: - "refactor this skill"
32: - "package this skill set"
33: 
34: **Secondary Triggers:**
35: - Detecting skill quality issues
36: - Identifying skill redundancy
37: - Planning skill migration
38: 
39: ## Core Philosophy
40: 
41: ### The Iron Law
42: 
43: > **NO SKILL WITHOUT A FAILING TEST FIRST**
44: 
45: Every skill must be validated against a real failure scenario before being written.
46: 
47: ### Knowledge Delta (The Core Formula)
48: 
49: > **Good Skill = Expert-only Knowledge − What Claude Already Knows**
50: 
51: A Skill's value is measured by its **knowledge delta** — the gap between what it provides and what the model already knows.
52: 
53: | Knowledge Type | Definition | Treatment |
54: |---------------|------------|-----------|
55: | **Expert** | Claude genuinely doesn't know this | MUST keep — this is the Skill's value |
56: | **Activation** | Claude knows but may not think of | Keep if brief — serves as reminder |
57: | **Redundant** | Claude definitely knows this | DELETE — wastes tokens |
58: 
59: **Evaluation**: For each section, ask "Does Claude already know this?"
60: 
61: ### Tool vs Skill
62: 
63: | Concept | Essence | Function |
64: |---------|---------|----------|
65: | **Tool** | What model CAN do | Execute actions (bash, read_file, write_file) |
66: | **Skill** | What model KNOWS how to do | Guide decisions (PDF processing, MCP building, frontend design) |
67: 
68: **Equation:** `General Agent + Excellent Skill = Domain Expert Agent`
69: 
70: ### The 5 Patterns System
71: 
72: | Pattern | ~Lines | Purpose | When to Use |
73: |---------|--------|---------|--------------|
74: | **Mindset** | ~50 | Thinking > technique, strong NEVER list | Creative tasks requiring taste |
75: | **Navigation** | ~30 | Minimal SKILL.md, routes to sub-files | Multiple distinct scenarios |
76: | **Philosophy** | ~150 | Philosophy → Express, emphasizes craft | Art/creation requiring originality |
77: | **Process** | ~200 | Phased workflow, checkpoints | Complex multi-step projects |
78: | **Tool** | ~300 | Decision trees, code examples | Precise operations on specific formats |
79: 
80: ### Progressive Disclosure
81: 
82: | Level | Content | When |
83: |-------|---------|------|
84: | **L1** | Metadata (name + description) | Always loaded (~100 tokens) |
85: | **L2** | SKILL.md body | On trigger match (~500 lines) |
86: | **L3** | references/, scripts/, templates/ | Explicit request |
87: 
88: ### Description — THE MOST IMPORTANT FIELD
89: 
90: The description determines if a skill ever gets activated. It MUST answer:
91: 
92: 1. **WHAT**: What does this Skill do?
93: 2. **WHEN**: In what situations should it be used?
94: 3. **KEYWORDS**: What terms should trigger this Skill?
95: 
96: ```
97: ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
98: │  SKILL ACTIVATION FLOW                                              │
99: │                                                                     │
100: │  User Request → Agent sees ALL skill descriptions → Decides which   │
101: │                 (only descriptions, not bodies!)      to activate    │
102: │                                                                     │
103: │  If description doesn't match → Skill NEVER gets loaded            │
104: │  If description is vague → Skill might not trigger when it should  │
105: └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
106: ```
107: 
108: **Excellent description format:**
109: ```yaml
110: description: >
111:   Create, edit, and analyze .docx files. 
112:   Use when working with Word documents, tracked changes, 
113:   or professional document formatting.
114:   Triggers: .docx, tracked changes, Word documents, document editing
115: ```
116: 
117: ### Freedom Calibration
118: 
119: Match specificity to task fragility:
120: 
121: | Task Type | Freedom | Why |
122: |-----------|---------|-----|
123: | Creative/Design | HIGH | Multiple valid approaches, differentiation is value |
124: | Code review | MEDIUM | Principles exist but judgment required |
125: | Precise operations | LOW | One wrong byte corrupts file, consistency critical |
126: 
127: ### TDD Workflow (RED-GREEN-REFACTOR)
128: 
129: **RED Phase:**
130: 1. Identify the failing scenario
131: 2. Write test prompt for the scenario
132: 3. Run without skill — observe failure
133: 4. Document exact failure mode
134: 
135: **GREEN Phase:**
136: 1. Write minimal skill addressing failure
137: 2. Run with skill — observe pass
138: 3. Verify failure mode resolved
139: 4. Document success criteria
140: 
141: **REFACTOR Phase:**
142: 1. Remove duplication
143: 2. Tighten trigger accuracy
144: 3. Ensure reference depth compliance
145: 4. Validate stacking ≤3
146: 
147: ## Skill-Judge Quality Metrics (120 points)
148: 
149: | Dimension | Max | Focus |
150: |-----------|-----|-------|
151: | **D1: Knowledge Delta** | 20 | Expert knowledge not in model |
152: | **D2: Mindset + Procedures** | 15 | Thinking patterns + domain workflows |
153: | **D3: Anti-Pattern Quality** | 15 | Specific NEVER lists with WHY |
154: | **D4: Spec Compliance** | 15 | Description = WHAT + WHEN + KEYWORDS |
155: | **D5: Progressive Disclosure** | 15 | Layering with triggers |
156: | **D6: Freedom Calibration** | 15 | Match specificity to fragility |
157: | **D7: Pattern Recognition** | 10 | Follows established pattern |
158: | **D8: Practical Usability** | 15 | Decision trees, fallbacks, edge cases |
159: 
160: ### Scoring
161: 
162: | Grade | Percentage | Meaning |
163: |-------|------------|---------|
164: | **A** | 90%+ (108+) | Excellent — production-ready |
165: | **B** | 80-89% (96-107) | Good — minor improvements |
166: | **C** | 70-79% (84-95) | Adequate — clear improvement path |
167: | **D** | 60-69% (72-83) | Below average — significant issues |
168: | **F** | <60% (<72) | Poor — fundamental redesign needed |
169: 
170: ### Quality Thresholds
171: 
172: | Score | Grade | Action |
173: |-------|-------|--------|
174: | 4.5+ | EXCELLENT | Ready for release |
175: | 4.0+ | GOOD | Minor improvements |
176: | 3.0+ | ACCEPTABLE | Address gaps |
177: | <3.0 | NEEDS WORK | Major revision required |
178: 
179: ## Context-Intelligence Integration
180: 
181: Every skill must integrate with context-intelligence:
182: 
183: - **Entry State Recognition**: Acknowledge session state
184: - **Trust Threshold**: Know minimum trust scores
185: - **Rot Detection**: Watch for degradation signals
186: - **Recovery Awareness**: Know when to escalate
187: 
188: ## Stacking Discipline
189: 
190: At entry, max **3 skills** may load:
191: 
192: ```
193: context-intelligence (1) — always
194: delegation-scope (1) — if delegated
195: workflow-hierarchy (1) — if workflow
196: context-rot-recovery (1) — if degraded
197: ```
198: 
199: **hivemind-skill-writer does not count** against stack (stacking: 0).
200: 
201: ## NEVER Do
202: 
203: - **NEVER** explain what Claude already knows ("what is X", "how to write a for-loop")
204: - **NEVER** give high scores for well-formatted but redundant content
205: - **NEVER** let length impress you — a 50-line Skill can outperform 500-line
206: - **NEVER** forgive vague descriptions — poor description = skill never triggers

2: name: workflow-coordination

4:   Orchestrates multi-phase workflows, manages phase transitions, validates milestone completion.

7:   - User says "execute plan", "run workflow", "complete phase"

30: 
31: # Workflow Coordination
32: 
33: Orchestrates multi-phase workflows from initiation through completion. Manages phase transitions with validation gates. Coordinates parallel execution when beneficial.
34: 
35: ## Philosophy
36: 
37: **GSD Principle:** Every workflow has phases. Skip phases at your own risk.
38: 
39: **Phase Workflows are NOT optional** for:
40: - New features with > 3 tasks
41: - Multi-file refactors
42: - Any task spanning > 1 hour
43: - Any task requiring testing
44: 
45: **Phase Workflows can be LIGHTWEIGHT for:**
46: - Quick fixes (< 15 min)
47: - Single file changes
48: - Documentation updates
49: - Research tasks
50: 
51: ## Standard Phase Sequence
52: 
53: ```
54: ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
55: │                    TYPICAL WORKFLOW                          │
56: ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
57: │                                                              │
58: │  DISCOVER   →   PLAN   →   EXECUTE   →   VERIFY   →  COMPLETE│
59: │    │            │           │             │               │
60: │    │            │           │             │               │
61: │    ▼            ▼           ▼             ▼               │
62: │ Context    Decompose   Implement     Validate          Document│
63: │ Assess     Tasks       Changes       Results         & Close │
64: │                                                              │
65: └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
66: ```
67: 
68: ## Phase Definitions
69: 
70: ### DISCOVER Phase
71: **Purpose:** Understand task scope, constraints, and context
72: 
73: **Activities:**
74: - Analyze user requirements
75: - Identify dependencies
76: - Assess complexity
77: - Map existing infrastructure
78: - Identify risks
79: 
80: **Exit Gate:** Clear problem statement with scope boundary
81: 
82: ### PLAN Phase
83: **Purpose:** Decompose into executable steps
84: 
85: **Activities:**
86: - Break into sequential/parallel tasks
87: - Estimate effort
88: - Define dependencies
89: - Set milestones
90: - Define success criteria
91: 
92: **Exit Gate:** Approved plan with measurable outcomes
93: 
94: ### EXECUTE Phase
95: **Purpose:** Implement changes
96: 
97: **Activities:**
98: - Make code changes
99: - Run tests
100: - Update documentation
101: - Seek clarification if needed
102: 
103: **Exit Gate:** All changes made, tests passing
104: 
105: ### VERIFY Phase
106: **Purpose:** Validate results against requirements
107: 
108: **Activities:**
109: - Run full test suite
110: - Verify against success criteria
111: - Check for regressions
112: - Validate user acceptance
113: 
114: **Exit Gate:** Confirmed by evidence
115: 
116: ### COMPLETE Phase
117: **Purpose:** Clean close and documentation
118: 
119: **Activities:**
120: - Document decisions
121: - Clean up artifacts
122: - Close milestone
123: - Summarize results
124: 
125: ## Transition Gates
126: 
127: Every phase transition requires gate validation:
128: 
129: ```
130: DISCOVER → PLAN: "Is scope clear? Are constraints known?"
131: PLAN → EXECUTE: "Is plan approved? Are dependencies resolved?"
132: EXECUTE → VERIFY: "Are changes complete? Is evidence ready?"
133: VERIFY → COMPLETE: "Do results meet criteria? Is user satisfied?"
134: ```
135: 
136: ### Gate Validation Checklist
137: 
138: | Gate | Question | Evidence Required |
139: |------|----------|-------------------|
140: | Discover→Plan | Scope clear? | Problem statement |
141: | Plan→Execute | Plan approved? | Task list, estimates |
142: | Execute→Verify | Changes done? | Code diff, test results |
143: | Verify→Complete | Criteria met? | Validation report |
144: 
145: ## FAIL Gates
146: 
147: **STOP IMMEDIATELY if:**
148: - Evidence of harm (data loss, security issue)
149: - Fundamental scope change
150: - Resource exhaustion
151: - User requests stop
152: 
153: ## Milestone Tracking
154: 
155: ### Milestone Structure
156: 
157: ```typescript
158: interface Milestone {
159:   id: string,
160:   name: string,
161:   phases: Phase[],
162:   status: 'pending' | 'active' | 'complete' | 'blocked',
163:   startedAt?: string,
164:   completedAt?: string,
165:   blockers?: string[],
166: }
167: ```
168: 
169: ### Milestone States
170: 
171: ```
172: PENDING → ACTIVE → COMPLETE
173:               ↓
174:            BLOCKED → (resolved) → ACTIVE
175: ```
176: 
177: ## Parallel Coordination
178: 
179: When EXECUTE phase benefits from parallelism:
180: 
181: ### Parallel Patterns
182: 
183: **Pattern 1: Embarrassingly Parallel**
184: ```
185: Task A → independent → Result A
186: Task B → independent → Result B
187: Task C → independent → Result C
188:          ↓
189:     MERGE Results
190: ```
191: 
192: **Pattern 2: Pipeline Parallel**
193: ```
194: Phase 1: A → B → C (sequential within phase)
195:                   ↓
196: Phase 2: D → E → F (can start when C done)
197: ```
198: 
199: **Pattern 3: Fan-out/Fan-in**
200: ```
201:         → Task B →
202: Task A →          → MERGE
203:         → Task C →
204: ```
205: 
206: ### Coordination Rules
207: 
208: 1. **Scope division** — Tasks must be independent
209: 2. **Merge strategy** — Who resolves conflicts
210: 3. **Communication** — How to share intermediate state
211: 4. **Failure handling** — What happens if one fails
212: 
213: ## NEVER Do
214: 
215: - Skip DISCOVER for complex tasks
216: - Skip VERIFY before COMPLETE
217: - Merge parallel results without conflict resolution
218: - Close milestone without user sign-off
219: - Skip gate validation to "save time"
220: 
221: ## Integration with context-intelligence
222: 
223: Workflow-Coordination runs AFTER context-intelligence:
224: 
225: | Entry State | Workflow Behavior |
226: |-------------|-------------------|
227: | FRESH | Normal workflow initiation |
228: | RESUMED | Resume from last incomplete phase |
229: | DELEGATED | Check delegation status before new workflow |
230: | DEGRADED | Use minimal workflow, heavy validation |
231: | POST-CANCEL | Clean close of canceled workflow |
232: | LATE | Prioritize verification over exploration |
233: 
234: ## See Also
235: 
236: - `references/01-phase-lifecycle.md` — Phase details
237: - `references/02-transition-gates.md` — Gate validation
238: - `references/03-milestone-tracking.md` — Milestone management
239: - `references/04-parallel-coordination.md` — Parallel execution

(End of file - total 239 lines)
</content>
```

# Conceptual model that must be preserved

## The philosophy of the skill system

The skill system must address granularity and variants while preserving domain specificity and deterministic patterns where appropriate.

It must be built around these 3 patterns:

### Pattern 1: high-level routing skill

A broad, high-level skill that helps route, frame, and stack other skills through references.

Example: `Hivemind-runtime-context`

This pattern should help determine:

- whether the session is user-facing or delegated
- workflow hierarchy
- project phase
- agent role context
- purpose and user intent
- context awareness checklist
- when to stack other skills
- when not to stack
- when to narrow to a more specific branch

This pattern is breadth-oriented and should support progressive disclosure without becoming vague.

### Pattern 2: classification- and domain-specific branch skills

These are narrower, more structured skills that classify the situation into a domain or workflow branch.

They can cross with Pattern 1 and should provide one level deeper guidance, such as:

- step-by-step workflow shape
- templates to use
- artifacts to inspect
- context types to gather
- ordering of analysis or execution
- phase-specific planning
- workflow-specific TDD guidance

These are not as broad as Pattern 1 and not as vertically deep as Pattern 3.

### Pattern 3: deep expertise / conditional vertical depth skills

These are used when the problem requires expert or sensitive depth.

They may stack with Pattern 1 and Pattern 2.

A clear example is a skill related to maintaining and auditing `AGENTS.md`, especially when:

- projects are simple or deeply nested
- context can be poisoned
- hierarchy can become misleading
- governance artifacts create conflicts
- audit or repair work requires careful authority resolution

Because Pattern 3 can become lengthy, it must use:

- TOC
- in-text jump links
- strongly organized sections
- constrained vertical depth

## Constraints on loading and composition

Design the pack with the understanding that:

- agents can load up to 3 skills per entry/turn
- there must still be room for other necessary skills in-session
- skill granularity must support selective loading
- session context pruning is possible
- skills must survive degraded context and still guide recovery

This means the plan must explicitly manage **degree of freedom** and avoid bloated, overly generic, or overly monolithic skills.

## Chaining and references

The pack must support intelligent chaining, but with strong limits:

- references should only be 1-level deep
- stacking should remain horizontal at the reference layer
- decisions to cross-skill must be explicit and justified
- Pattern 3 references must not dump excessive text inline
- use TOCs and jump links for deeper branches
- assets may include templates, examples, diagrams, and standards

## Examples of cross-skill chaining to account for

Include examples such as:

- context as governance → `AGENTS.md` maintenance skill
- use-case skills → delegation skill
- cross-case scenario → delegation + tech research
- deep codebase investigation + tech research → linked to tech synthesis
- domain-specific workflow skills + evaluation steps + planning/TDD templates

These are examples of the mindset, not the final limit of the system.

---

# Specific plan focus: Context Intelligence Pack

## Pattern 1 anchor skill

The pack must include the high-level routing skill for context intelligence, for example:

- `Hivemind-runtime-context`

This should serve as the top-level entry skill for context-aware routing and skill stacking.

## Design principles to embed in the pack and its skills

Design the pack with the mindset that context intelligence improves when hierarchy, order, depth, and breadth are respected across project entities.

The skills should promote:

- hierarchy-aware reading and execution
- awareness of both breadth and depth
- support across the full project lifecycle
- consistency across meta concepts, documents, governance, tests, delegation, and workflows
- naming consistency
- non-breaking YAML frontmatter
- in-text jump links and TOCs
- sharding long documents into numbered files with `index.md`
- safe scripting guidance
- regex-based matching where appropriate
- pattern awareness instead of brittle absolutes
- non-singular, non-fragile heuristics

## Safe operational practices to include

The plan and the resulting skills should also promote:

- atomic git commits for planning and coding tasks
- using `.worktrees` and branches when appropriate
- awareness that meta-frameworks differ
- awareness that coding platforms differ

## Underdeveloped factors that must now be addressed properly

The revised plan must explicitly address:

- promoting hierarchy for both AI agents and humans
- safe code tree inspection
- shell commands that show the project tree while excluding `node_modules`, cache, build artifacts, and similar noise
- discovery and exploration scripts only by default, not risky mutation scripts
- multi-environment script patterns
- regex instead of absolute paths where possible
- fuzzy matching where appropriate
- git usage for atomic changes and context mapping
- techniques for mapping long-term and historical context
- time and date awareness when deciding conflicts between same-level entities
- prioritizing the latest valid same-level authority only when logically justified

---

# What the revised plan must accomplish

Produce a plan that clearly defines:

## 1. Pack architecture

- the full architecture of the Context Intelligence Pack
- how it relates to the wider Hivemind skill-pack ecosystem
- which skills belong in Pattern 1, Pattern 2, and Pattern 3
- what should remain separate versus bundled
- what should be references only versus embedded content
- how the pack should evolve over milestones and branches

## 2. Branching and conditional variants

Define the skeletal branch structure and the conditional branches for possible variants or future expansions.

Be explicit about:

- main branch themes
- milestone branches
- experimental branches
- framework-specific branches if needed
- conditional expansion paths based on evaluation results
- what can be added later without destabilizing the core pack

## 3. Progressive disclosure and degree-of-freedom control

Show how the plan narrows correctly from broad entry to specific use without becoming rigid or confusing.

This must cover:

- front-facing agent entry
- multiple entry points
- agent roles
- main sessions vs sub-sessions
- workflow hierarchy
- project phases
- situations that require stacking
- situations that require branching
- situations that require not loading extra skills

## 4. Skill-writing and skill-auditing guidance

The plan must support not only this project’s current pack, but also future skill writing by end users.

This includes guidance for:

- writing new skills in the Hivemind ecosystem
- auditing skills to avoid conflicts
- preventing “dumb deterministic” behavior
- avoiding overlap and duplication
- preventing selection confusion
- preventing collisions with planning/TDD skills
- preventing meta-framework clashes
- deciding whether to refactor, consolidate, migrate, keep, or remove a skill

This is especially important for the Hivemind skill writer and any audit-oriented skill.

## 5. TDD and evaluation strategy

The plan must incorporate TDD-oriented skill development and evaluation.

Include how to:

- define testable expectations for skills
- evaluate packs and individual skills
- track effectiveness over time
- use evaluation to decide pack changes
- stress test skills under:
  - context rot
  - partial or pruned context
  - mixed frameworks
  - cross-skill loading
  - end-user environments

Also explain when proven skills should later become reference skills with templates and chain links.

## 6. Naming, packaging, and documentation standards

Align the plan with the naming and planning documentation.

Be explicit about:

- naming principles for packs and skills
- bundle structure
- assessment/evaluation alignment
- how long documents should be sharded
- index structure
- frontmatter stability
- references, templates, and assets organization

## 7. Theme-setting and anti-chaos intent

Use the “setting the theme” context carefully.

The revised plan must show how the skill packages are meant to improve intelligence and flexibility rather than worsen confusion.

It must explicitly guard against:

- shallow skills that add noise
- loading too many vague skills
- framework confusion
- false confidence
- token waste
- nonsensical or low-value testing
- agents acting without sufficient context intelligence
- governance or hierarchy collapse

---

# Writing and tone requirements for the resulting plan and for the skills it proposes

Write so the eventual skills are:

- encouraging and confidence-building
- protective of user workflows and project integrity
- logically reasoned
- educational where needed
- aware of complex project environments
- aware of collaborative, domain-specific, multi-agent work
- strict when dealing with deterministic or genuinely authoritative elements
- explicit about gaps, uncertainty, and edge cases
- cautionary about hallucination risk
- professional and consistent

Balance these tensions correctly:

- breadth vs specificity
- concision vs completeness
- governance vs flexibility
- deterministic language vs mixed or unknown realities
- strict instruction vs adaptive reasoning

When writing high-level skills, cover breadth.

When narrowing degree of freedom, explain the niche clearly and compare when to use which pattern or branch.

Concision must not remove specificity. Precision must not pretend unknown variables do not exist.

The system must remain robust across different model families, including models that:

- are principle-driven but can become rigid
- need tighter constraints to avoid overdoing actions
- prefer concise instructions but underperform if underspecified

---

Return a structured plan with clear hierarchy and strong sectioning.

   - how to avoid conflicts and brittle determinism

   - quality metrics
   - testing approach

8. **Documentation and packaging standards**
   - naming

   - TOCs

9. **Operational safeguards**

10. **Refactor / consolidate / migrate / remove framework**

    - concrete immediate next steps
    - what should be drafted first
    - what should be validated before expansion

149: 
150: # 3. CONTEXT-INTELLIGENCE ARCHITECTURE
151: 
152: ## 3.1 Design Principles
153: 
154: ```
155: ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
156: │                    CONTEXT-INTELLIGENCE ENTRY PACK              │
157: ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
158: │  Primary Goal: Defense against context rot, pollution, poisoning │
159: │  Secondary: Non-breaking harness boosting for agent intelligence │
160: │  Tertiary:  Foundation for specialized workflow packs             │
161: └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
162: ```
163: 
164: ### 3.1.1 Entry Pack Structure
165: 
166: ```
167: context-intelligence/
168: ├── SKILL.md                    # MUST-LOAD entry skill
169: ├── references/
170: │   ├── context-rot-taxonomy.md  # Severity model + detection
171: │   ├── entry-state-matrix.md   # Session state awareness
172: │   ├── delegation-scope.md     # Subagent scope rules
173: │   └── platform-surface.md     # Cross-platform awareness
174: ├── scripts/
175: │   ├── detect-rot.sh           # Context rot detection
176: │   └── assess-trust.sh         # Trust scoring
177: └── bundles/
178:     ├── hierarchy-rules.md      # Project hierarchy awareness
179:     └── workflow-relay.md       # Workflow coordination
180: ```
181: 
182: ### 3.1.2 Progressive Disclosure Loading
183: 
184: | Trigger Condition | Load Level | Content |
185: |-----------------|------------|---------|
186: | Every session start | L1 (~100 words) | Core entry skill overview + context-rot warning |
187: | When delegation detected | L2 (+200 words) | Delegation scope + authority rules |
188: | When workflow invoked | L3 (+300 words) | Hierarchy + workflow coordination |
189: | When context drift suspected | L4 (+ref) | Full context rot model + recovery |
190: | When platform mismatch | L5 (+ref) | Cross-platform surface awareness |
191: 
192: ## 3.2 Must-Load Entry Skill Core
193: 
194: ### SKILL.md Structure (L1 — Always Loaded)
195: 
196: ```yaml
197: ---
198: name: context-intelligence-entry
199: description: Use when starting a session, resuming after interruption, detecting context drift, or when delegation scope is unclear. Defends against context rot, pollution, and poisoning in multi-agent IDE environments.
200: ---
201: 
202: # Context-Intelligence Entry Pack
203: 
204: ## Overview
205: This pack provides always-activated context defense for agentic IDE workflows.
206: 
207: ## Core Principles
208: 
209: 1. **Skeptical Reading** — Trust but verify all inherited context
210: 2. **Hierarchy Awareness** — Know your authority scope at all times  
211: 3. **Entry State Awareness** — Recognize where you are in the session lifecycle
212: 4. **Delegation Clarity** — Understand inherited vs. own scope
213: 5. **Rot Detection** — Watch for context degradation signals
214: 
215: ## Context Rot Defense (Always Active)
216: 
217: ### Detection Signals
218: - Document timestamps contradict recent actions
219: - Governance files reference non-existent entities
220: - Skills load unexpectedly or contradict each other
221: - Session state doesn't match observable reality
222: - Delegation scope is ambiguous or conflicting
223: 
224: ### Response Protocol
225: 1. **STOP** — Do not assume
226: 2. **ASSESS** — Check context integrity signals  
227: 3. **VERIFY** — Run discovery commands to confirm
228: 4. **CONFIRM** — Ask user before high-impact actions
229: 5. **RECOVER** — Use safe recovery paths
230: 
231: ## Entry State Matrix
232: 
233: | State | Indicators | Required Action |
234: |-------|------------|-----------------|
235: | NEW SESSION | First message, fresh context | Full context map |
236: | RESUMED | Mid-session continuation | Verify prior state |
237: | DEGRADED | Pruned context, gaps | Assess damage |
238: | DELEGATED | Subagent context | Verify scope |
239: | RECOVERED | Post-interruption | Re-establish truth |
240: 
241: ## Hierarchy Rules
242: 
243: 1. **Authority**: Source authority > Project authority > Inherited authority
244: 2. **Freshness**: Latest same-level authority when logically justified
245: 3. **Scope**: Own scope > Inherited scope — always know the boundary
246: 4. **Pattern over Absolutes**: Regex > hardcoded paths
247: 
248: ## Safe Practices
249: 
250: - Atomic commits for plan + code pairs
251: - `.worktree` for isolation when uncertain
252: - Discovery scripts only (never mutating by default)
253: - Time/date awareness for conflict resolution
254: ```
255: 
256: ## 3.3 Subskill Branching
257: 
258: ### Branch A: Delegation Intelligence
259: 
260: ```yaml
261: description: Use when delegating to subagents or when receiving delegated scope.
262: ```
263: 
264: **Scope Inheritance Rules:**
265: - Inherit: task description, constraints, success criteria
266: - Do NOT Inherit: parent session state, unrelated context
267: - Always: declare scope boundaries explicitly
268: 
269: ### Branch B: Workflow Coordination
270: 
271: ```yaml
272: description: Use when executing granular, relational, hierarchical workflows.
273: ```
274: 
275: **Hierarchy Rules:**
276: - Planning → Implementation → Verification → Delivery
277: - Numbered documents with `index.md` for sharded content
278: - TOC + in-text jumps for navigation
279: 
280: ### Branch C: Context Rot Recovery
281: 
282: ```yaml
283: description: Use when context degradation, pollution, or poisoning is suspected.
284: ```
285: 
286: **Recovery Protocol:**
287: 1. Isolate suspicious context
288: 2. Rebuild from authoritative sources
289: 3. Verify with user confirmation
290: 4. Document recovery path
291: 
292: ---
293: 
294: # 4. CONTEXT ROT DEFENSE MODEL
295: 
296: ## 4.1 Definition
297: 
298: **Context Rot** = Gradual degradation of context integrity leading to:
299: - Stale governance signals
300: - Outdated artifact references
301: - Conflicting authority claims
302: - Degraded mid-session state
303: 
304: **Context Pollution** = Introduction of misleading, false, or conflicting context:
305: - Wrong file references
306: - Fake authority signals
307: - Manipulated artifact chains
308: 
309: **Context Poisoning** = Deliberate or accidental injection of:
310: - Misleading documentation
311: - False test assertions
312: - Fake governance entities
313: 
314: ## 4.2 Severity Taxonomy
315: 
316: | Level | Name | Detection | Response |
317: |-------|------|----------|----------|
318: | 0 | CLEAN | All signals consistent | Continue normal ops |
319: | 1 | SUSPECT | Minor inconsistencies | Note, verify before critical actions |
320: | 2 | DEGRADED | Significant drift | Pause, assess, recover |
321: | 3 | POLLUTED | Major conflicts | Stop, isolate, rebuild |
322: | 4 | POISONED | Dangerous/malicious | Emergency isolation, user alert |
323: 
324: ## 4.3 Detection Dimensions
325: 
326: ### D1: Governance Integrity
327: - [ ] All referenced files exist
328: - [ ] AGENTS.md references are current
329: - [ ] Skill triggers match actual content
330: - [ ] Authority signals are legitimate
331: 
332: ### D2: Temporal Consistency  
333: - [ ] Document timestamps align with git history
334: - [ ] Recent changes reflected in context
335: - [ ] No future-dated stale artifacts
336: - [ ] Same-level authority conflict resolution is logical
337: 
338: ### D3: Delegation Scope
339: - [ ] Delegation chain is traceable
340: - [ ] Scope boundaries are explicit
341: - [ ] No scope creep or bleeding
342: - [ ] Parent-child relationships are clear
343: 
344: ### D4: Workflow Integrity
345: - [ ] Planning → Implementation → Verification flow is intact
346: - [ ] No orphaned artifacts
347: - [ ] Test assertions match implementation
348: - [ ] Handoff points are clean
349: 
350: ### D5: Platform Surface
351: - [ ] Platform-specific paths are correct
352: - [ ] Cross-platform awareness is accurate
353: - [ ] No phantom file/directory references
354: - [ ] Symlinks resolve correctly
355: 
356: ## 4.4 Trust Evaluation Matrix
357: 
358: | Signal | Trust Score | Weight |
359: |--------|-------------|--------|
360: | Live SDK/plugin behavior | 100% | 1.0 |
361: | User confirmation | 100% | 1.0 |
362: | Git-verified file | 95% | 0.9 |
363: | Type-checked code | 90% | 0.8 |
364: | Documentation | 50% | 0.5 |
365: | Inherited context | 40% | 0.4 |
366: | Unverified claims | 10% | 0.1 |
367: | Contradictory signals | 0% | 0.0 |
368: 
369: **Formula:** `Effective Trust = Σ(Signal × Weight) / Σ(Weight)`
370: 
371: **Threshold:** If Effective Trust < 0.6 → Context Rot suspected
372: 
373: ## 4.5 Recovery Handling
374: 
375: ### Recovery Protocol Alpha (Self-Recovery)
376: 
377: 1. Isolate suspicious context
378: 2. Rebuild from nearest clean source
379: 3. Cross-verify with git history
380: 4. Continue if trust > 0.7
381: 
382: ### Recovery Protocol Beta (User-Assisted)
383: 
384: 1. Stop execution
385: 2. Present evidence of rot
386: 3. Request user confirmation
387: 4. Follow user guidance
388: 
389: ### Recovery Protocol Gamma (Emergency)
390: 
391: 1. Halt all actions
392: 2. Alert user with evidence
393: 3. Await explicit instruction
394: 4. Document incident
395: 
396: ## 4.6 Confirmation Thresholds
397: 
398: | Action Impact | Required Trust | Confirmation |
399: |--------------|----------------|--------------|
400: | Read files | 0.4 | None |
401: | Write files | 0.6 | User if < 0.7 |
402: | Delete files | 0.8 | User confirmation |
403: | Execute commands | 0.7 | User if < 0.8 |
404: | Delegation | 0.6 | Explicit scope declaration |
405: | Claim completion | 0.8 | Evidence presented |
406: 
407: ---
408: 
409: # 5. CONTEXT-INTELLIGENCE SKILL PACKAGE DRAFT
410: 
411: ## 5.1 Primary Entry Skill
412: 
413: **File:** `skills/context-intelligence/SKILL.md`
414: 
415: ```yaml
416: ---
417: name: context-intelligence-entry
418: description: Use at session start, after compaction, when detecting drift, or when delegation scope is unclear. Provides context rot defense, hierarchy awareness, and trust evaluation for multi-agent IDE environments. Works with any framework (OpenCode, Claude Code, Cursor, etc.) — framework selection is situational.
419: ---
420: 
421: # Context-Intelligence Entry Pack
422: 
423: ## Purpose
424: Always-activated defense against context rot, pollution, and poisoning in complex IDE-based, multi-agent, multi-workflow environments.
425: 
426: ## When to Activate
427: 
428: **L1 (Always):** On every session start, resume, or continuation
429: **L2 (On Delegation):** When receiving or granting delegated scope  
430: **L3 (On Workflow):** When executing granular, relational workflows
431: **L4 (On Suspicion):** When context degradation signals detected
432: 
433: ## Core Protocol
434: 
435: ### CONTEXT ROT DEFENSE (Never Skip)
436: 
437: 1. **OBSERVE** — Note all context signals before acting
438: 2. **ASSESS** — Score trust using the Trust Matrix (see reference)
439: 3. **VERIFY** — Run discovery if signals inconsistent
440: 4. **CONFIRM** — User confirmation for high-impact actions
441: 5. **RECOVER** — Follow recovery protocol if trust < 0.6
442: 
443: ### Hierarchy Awareness
444: 
445: - **Source Authority** > **Project Authority** > **Inherited Authority**
446: - **Latest Valid Same-Level Authority** when logically justified
447: - **Own Scope** > **Inherited Scope** — always know boundary
448: - **Pattern Matching** > **Hardcoded Paths** — prefer regex where safe
449: 
450: ### Entry State Recognition
451: 
452: | State | Indicators | Action |
453: |-------|------------|--------|
454: | `NEW` | First message, fresh context | Full context map |
455: | `RESUMED` | Mid-session, prior state exists | Verify continuity |
456: | `DEGRADED` | Pruned, gaps, inconsistencies | Assess damage |
457: | `DELEGATED` | Subagent context | Verify inherited scope |
458: | `INTERRUPTED` | Post-cancellation, partial state | Re-establish truth |
459: 
460: ### Delegation Scope Rules
461: 
462: **INHERIT:** Task, constraints, success criteria
463: **DO NOT INHERIT:** Parent session state, unrelated context
464: **ALWAYS:** Declare scope boundaries explicitly
465: 
466: ### Safe Operational Patterns
467: 
468: - **Atomic commits**: Plan + code pairs together
469: - **Worktree isolation**: When uncertain, use `.worktree`
470: - **Discovery first**: Scripts must be read-only by default
471: - **Time awareness**: Date conflict resolution favors latest valid
472: - **No absolutes**: Prefer patterns, regex, fuzzy matching
473: 
474: ## Context Rot Detection Signals
475: 
476: If ANY of these appear, ASSESS before proceeding:
477: - Document timestamps contradict git history
478: - Governance files reference non-existent entities
479: - Skills load unexpectedly or contradict
480: - Session state doesn't match observable reality
481: - Authority claims conflict at same level
482: - Tests pass but implementation is broken
483: 
484: ## Response Protocol
485: 
486: | Severity | Condition | Action |
487: |----------|-----------|--------|
488: | 0 (Clean) | All signals consistent | Continue |
489: | 1 (Suspect) | Minor inconsistencies | Verify before critical actions |
490: | 2 (Degraded) | Significant drift | Pause, assess, recover |
491: | 3 (Polluted) | Major conflicts | Stop, isolate, rebuild |
492: | 4 (Poisoned) | Dangerous signals | Emergency isolation, alert user |
493: 
494: ## High-Impact Action Gates
495: 
496: | Action | Trust Required | Confirmation |
497: |--------|---------------|---------------|
498: | Read files | 0.4 | None |
499: | Write files | 0.6 | User if < 0.7 |
500: | Delete files | 0.8 | Always confirm |
501: | Execute commands | 0.7 | User if < 0.8 |
502: | Delegate | 0.6 | Explicit scope |
503: | Claim completion | 0.8 | Evidence required |
504: 
505: ## References
506: 
507: - `references/context-rot-taxonomy.md` — Full severity model
508: - `references/entry-state-matrix.md` — Session state details
509: - `references/delegation-scope.md` — Scope rules
510: - `references/trust-matrix.md` — Scoring system
511: - `references/platform-surface.md` — Cross-platform awareness
512: ```
513: 
514: ## 5.2 Reference: Context Rot Taxonomy
515: 
516: **File:** `skills/context-intelligence/references/context-rot-taxonomy.md`
517: 
518: ```markdown
519: # Context Rot Taxonomy
520: 
521: ## Severity Levels
522: 
523: ### Level 0: CLEAN
524: All context signals are consistent with authoritative sources.
525: 
526: **Indicators:**
527: - All file references resolve
528: - Governance documents align
529: - Timestamps consistent with git
530: - Delegation chains are traceable
531: 
532: **Response:** Continue normal operations
533: 
534: ---
535: 
536: ### Level 1: SUSPECT
537: Minor inconsistencies that don't affect core functionality.
538: 
539: **Indicators:**
540: - 1-2 minor timestamp mismatches
541: - Single document reference could be stale
542: - Minor cosmetic inconsistencies
543: 
544: **Response:** Note and verify before critical actions
545: 
546: ---
547: 
548: ### Level 2: DEGRADED
549: Significant context drift affecting workflow coherence.
550: 
551: **Indicators:**
552: - Multiple timestamp conflicts
553: - Some referenced files don't exist
554: - Delegation scope unclear
555: - Test assertions don't match code
556: - Gap in session history
557: 
558: **Response:** Pause, perform full context assessment, recover
559: 
560: ---
561: 
562: ### Level 3: POLLUTED
563: Major conflicts that break trust in context integrity.
564: 
565: **Indicators:**
566: - Conflicting authority claims at same level
567: - Governance references non-existent entities
568: - Skill triggers contradict each other
569: - Significant gap in session state
570: - Tests pass but implementation clearly broken
571: 
572: **Response:** Stop execution, isolate polluted context, rebuild from authoritative sources
573: 
574: ---
575: 
576: ### Level 4: POISONED
577: Dangerous or potentially malicious context injection.
578: 
579: **Indicators:**
580: - Authority claims that are demonstrably false
581: - Test assertions that pass but encode wrong behavior
582: - Governance that would cause harmful actions
583: - Manipulated git history signals
584: - Deliberate misdirection in artifacts
585: 
586: **Response:** EMERGENCY STOP. Alert user immediately. Await explicit instruction.
587: 
588: ---
589: 
590: ## Detection Checklist
591: 
592: ### D1: Governance Integrity
593: - [ ] All referenced files exist
594: - [ ] AGENTS.md references current
595: - [ ] Skill triggers match content
596: - [ ] Authority signals are legitimate
597: 
598: ### D2: Temporal Consistency
599: - [ ] Timestamps align with git history
600: - [ ] Recent changes in context
601: - [ ] No future-dated artifacts
602: - [ ] Same-level authority resolved logically
603: 
604: ### D3: Delegation Scope
605: - [ ] Chain traceable
606: - [ ] Boundaries explicit
607: - [ ] No scope creep
608: - [ ] Parent-child clear
609: 
610: ### D4: Workflow Integrity
611: - [ ] P→I→V→D flow intact
612: - [ ] No orphaned artifacts
613: - [ ] Tests match implementation
614: - [ ] Handoffs clean
615: 
616: ### D5: Platform Surface
617: - [ ] Paths correct for platform
618: - [ ] Cross-platform awareness accurate
619: - [ ] No phantom references
620: - [ ] Symlinks resolve
621: ```
622: 
623: ## 5.3 Reference: Entry State Matrix
624: 
625: **File:** `skills/context-intelligence/references/entry-state-matrix.md`
626: 
627: ```markdown
628: # Entry State Matrix
629: 
630: ## Session Lifecycle States
631: 
632: ### NEW SESSION
633: **Definition:** First message of a new OpenCode session
634: 
635: **Indicators:**
636: - No prior context in current conversation
637: - Fresh session ID
638: - No `.hivemind/` state for this session
639: 
640: **Required Actions:**
641: 1. Map project context
642: 2. Identify authoritative surfaces
643: 3. Note any pre-existing state
644: 4. Establish baseline trust score
645: 
646: ---
647: 
648: ### RESUMED SESSION  
649: **Definition:** Continuation after natural context window
650: 
651: **Indicators:**
652: - Prior context exists but may be pruned
653: - Gap in conversation history
654: - Session ID continues
655: 
656: **Required Actions:**
657: 1. Verify prior state markers
658: 2. Check for gaps in trajectory
659: 3. Re-establish continuity
660: 4. Assess context completeness
661: 
662: ---
663: 
664: ### DEGRADED SESSION
665: **Definition:** State where context integrity is compromised
666: 
667: **Indicators:**
668: - Pruned context window
669: - Missing mid-session artifacts
670: - Unclear what preceded current state
671: - Contradictory signals
672: 
673: **Required Actions:**
674: 1. STOP assuming prior state is accurate
675: 2. Rebuild context from authoritative sources
676: 3. Verify key facts independently
677: 4. Score trust level
678: 
679: ---
680: 
681: ### DELEGATED SESSION
682: **Definition:** Subagent or child session with inherited scope
683: 
684: **Indicators:**
685: - Received delegated task
686: - Explicit scope declaration present
687: - Working within boundaries
688: 
689: **Required Actions:**
690: 1. Understand inherited vs. own scope
691: 2. Verify delegation chain
692: 3. Do NOT inherit parent session state
693: 4. Stay within declared boundaries
694: 
695: ---
696: 
697: ### INTERRUPTED SESSION
698: **Definition:** Resumed after cancellation or error
699: 
700: **Indicators:**
701: - Prior action was incomplete
702: - No clear outcome from previous turn
703: - State may be partially written
704: 
705: **Required Actions:**
706: 1. Assess what completed vs. what didn't
707: 2. Verify state integrity
708: 3. Resume or restart as appropriate
709: 4. Document any ambiguity
710: 
711: ---
712: 
713: ### RECOVERED SESSION
714: **Definition:** After successful context repair
715: 
716: **Indicators:**
717: - Context integrity restored
718: - Trust score returned to normal
719: - Prior issues documented
720: 
721: **Required Actions:**
722: 1. Verify restoration
723: 2. Continue with confidence
724: 3. Document recovery path
725: ```
726: 
727: ## 5.4 Reference: Delegation Scope
728: 
729: **File:** `skills/context-intelligence/references/delegation-scope.md`
730: 
731: ```markdown
732: # Delegation Scope Rules
733: 
734: ## Scope Inheritance Matrix
735: 
736: | Element | Inherit? | Rationale |
737: |---------|----------|-----------|
738: | Task description | YES | Core mandate |
739: | Constraints | YES | Operating bounds |
740: | Success criteria | YES | Target definition |
741: | Parent session state | NO | Privacy, isolation |
742: | Unrelated context | NO | Scope containment |
743: | Authority to delegate further | NO | Chain of command |
744: | Parent's internal doubts | NO | Noise reduction |
745: 
746: ## Scope Declaration Protocol
747: 
748: When receiving delegation:
749: ```
750: SCOPE DECLARATION:
751: - Task: [specific task]
752: - Constraints: [bounds]
753: - Success: [measurable outcome]
754: - Duration: [expected scope lifetime]
755: - Boundaries: [what is NOT in scope]
756: ```
757: 
758: When granting delegation:
759: ```
760: SCOPE GRANT:
761: - Agent: [subagent identifier]
762: - Task: [specific task]
763: - Constraints: [bounds + authority level]
764: - Success: [measurable outcome]
765: - Reporting: [how to report back]
766: ```
767: 
768: ## Chain of Command
769: 
770: 1. **ORIGINAL AUTHORITY** — User or top-level agent
771: 2. **PRIMARY DELEGATOR** — First-level delegate with full context
772: 3. **SUBAGENT** — Limited scope, task-specific
773: 
774: **Rule:** Each level can only delegate what it received + its own level additions
775: 
776: ## Anti-Patterns
777: 
778: ### Scope Bleed
779: - Parent context leaking into subagent
780: - Subagent acting on parent's unrelated tasks
781: - Unclear boundaries causing mixed outputs
782: 
783: ### Scope Creep
784: - Subagent taking initiative beyond granted scope
785: - Adding tasks not in original delegation
786: - Extending duration beyond specified
787: 
788: ### Scope Abandonment
789: - Subagent ignoring constraints
790: - Acting without reporting
791: - Abandoning task mid-execution
792: ```
793: 
794: ---
795: 
796: # 6. META-BUILDER SKILL DRAFT
797: 
798: **File:** `skills/meta-builder-hivemind/SKILL.md`
799: 
800: ```yaml
801: ---
802: name: meta-builder-hivemind
803: description: Use when creating, auditing, refactoring, or packaging HiveMind framework skills. Bundles context-intelligence frame, skill-writing guidance, audit methodology, and Hivemind-specific packaging patterns.
804: ---
805: 
806: # Meta-Builder: HiveMind Framework Skill Authoring
807: 
808: ## Purpose
809: Framework for creating high-quality skills specific to the HiveMind/OpenCode ecosystem.
810: 
811: ## When to Use
812: 
813: - Creating new skills for HiveMind
814: - Refactoring existing skills
815: - Auditing skill quality
816: - Packaging skill sets
817: - Designing cross-framework skills
818: 
819: ## Core Philosophy
820: 
821: ### TDD for Skills (RED-GREEN-REFACTOR)
822: 
823: | Phase | Action |
824: |-------|--------|
825: | RED | Write failing test prompt, observe baseline behavior |
826: | GREEN | Write minimal skill addressing specific failures |
827: | REFACTOR | Close loopholes, add explicit counters |
828: 
829: ### Iron Law
830: > NO SKILL WITHOUT A FAILING TEST FIRST
831: 
832: ### Progressive Disclosure
833: 
834: ```
835: L1: Metadata (name + description) — Always loaded (~100 words)
836: L2: SKILL.md body — On trigger (<500 lines)
837: L3: Bundled resources — As needed (scripts, references)
838: ```
839: 
840: ## Skill Anatomy
841: 
842: ```
843: skill-name/
844: ├── SKILL.md              # Required entry point
845: ├── references/           # Heavy documentation
846: │   ├── topic-a.md
847: │   └── topic-b.md
848: ├── scripts/              # Executable tools
849: └── templates/            # Reusable templates
850: ```
851: 
852: ## SKILL.md Frontmatter
853: 
854: ```yaml
855: ---
856: name: skill-name-with-hyphens
857: description: Use when [specific triggering conditions] — third person, max 1024 chars
858: ---
859: ```
860: 
861: **Description Rules:**
862: - Start with "Use when..."
863: - Include specific symptoms, situations, contexts
864: - NO workflow summary in description
865: - Third person perspective
866: - Under 500 characters if possible
867: 
868: ## Quality Checklist
869: 
870: ### Before Writing
871: - [ ] Is this a reusable pattern?
872: - [ ] Would I reference this across projects?
873: - [ ] Is it broader than project-specific?
874: - [ ] Can automation handle the mechanical parts?
875: 
876: ### During Writing
877: - [ ] Name uses letters, numbers, hyphens only
878: - [ ] Description triggers on specific conditions
879: - [ ] Overview states core principle in 1-2 sentences
880: - [ ] Includes "when NOT to use"
881: - [ ] Has one excellent example (not multi-language)
882: - [ ] Quick reference table for scanning
883: 
884: ### After Writing
885: - [ ] Run baseline test without skill
886: - [ ] Document exact rationalizations
887: - [ ] Write skill addressing those failures
888: - [ ] Re-test with skill
889: - [ ] Verify agents comply
890: 
891: ## Cross-Framework Considerations
892: 
893: When designing skills for multi-framework environments:
894: 
895: 1. **Situational selection** — pick the right framework per actual situation
896: 2. **No naming dogma** — don't force framework based on naming conventions
897: 3. **User intent respect** — follow what the user asks for, not what the framework dictates
898: 4. **Verification flexibility** — gates at user-specified points, not ritual
899: 5. **Authority clarity** — state what each framework owns in its domain
900: 
901: ## References
902: 
903: - `references/skill-quality-matrix.md` — Scoring dimensions
904: - `references/triple-pattern.md` — Stack/branch/conditional patterns
905: - `references/progressive-disclosure.md` — Loading strategy
906: - `references/auditing-protocol.md` — Skill audit methodology
907: ```
908: 
909: ---
910: 
911: # 7. TDD VERIFICATION PLAN
912: 
913: ## 7.1 Test Scenarios (Situational — Not Framework-Constrained)
914: 
915: These are **illustrative patterns** for verification methodology. Framework selection should follow the actual situation:
916: 
917: - Session type (new, resumed, delegated, degraded)
918: - User needs (verification at certain points, not ritual)
919: - Workflow requirements (planning → implementation → verification)
920: - Not constrained by naming conventions or single-framework dogma
921: 
922: ### Scenario 1: Planning Phase — Fresh Context
923: ```
924: Input: User wants to plan a feature, fresh session
925: Expected:
926:   - Agent maps project context
927:   - Identifies authoritative surfaces for planning
928:   - Checks relevant governance for this session type
929:   - Asks where user wants verification gates (if anywhere)
930: Validation: Planning mode activated, not default execution mode
931: ```
932: 
933: ### Scenario 2: Implementation — User-Specified Verification Gates
934: ```
935: Input: User specifies "verify before I commit" at certain points
936: Expected:
937:   - Agent respects verification gate points
938:   - Runs actual verification when gate reached
939:   - Asks for confirmation at gates, not on every action
940: Validation: Verification happens at user-specified points only
941: ```
942: 
943: ### Scenario 3: Delegation — Scope Without Ceremony
944: ```
945: Input: User delegates a subtask, expects autonomous execution
946: Expected:
947:   - Subagent receives clear scope declaration
948:   - Understands boundaries (included/excluded)
949:   - Reports at specified points, not constant check-ins
950: Validation: Scope boundaries respected, no ceremony overhead
951: ```
952: 
953: ### Scenario 4: Resumed Session — Continuity Without Hallucination
954: ```
955: Input: User says "continue where we left off" after a gap
956: Expected:
957:   - Agent verifies what was actually completed
958:   - Rebuilds context from last known good state
959:   - Proceeds only after confirming continuity
960: Validation: No hallucinated progress, real state acknowledged
961: ```
962: 
963: ### Scenario 5: Evidence Request — Proof Over Claims
964: ```
965: Input: User asks "show me this actually works"
966: Expected:
967:   - Agent presents verifiable command output
968:   - Runs verification commands, shows real results
969:   - Evidence is evidence-output-based, not assertion
970: Validation: Proof is command-output, not "I verified it"
971: ```
972: 
973: ### Scenario 6: Mixed Framework — Situational Selection
974: ```
975: Input: Project has elements from multiple frameworks (normal in practice)
976: Expected:
977:   - Agent recognizes which framework applies in which situation
978:   - Doesn't force single-framework dogma
979:   - Respects user intent for workflow selection
980: Validation: Appropriate selection per situation, not naming rules
981: ```
982: 
983: ### Scenario 7: Drift Detection — Stop Before Harm
984: ```
985: Input: Agent detects claimed state doesn't match reality
986: Expected:
987:   - Stops assuming
988:   - Presents evidence of mismatch
989:   - Asks for clarification before continuing
990: Validation: No blind continuation when signals conflict
991: ```
992: 
993: ### Scenario 8: Degraded Recovery — User Confirms Path
994: ```
995: Input: Session in bad state, user asks to recover
996: Expected:
997:   - Agent presents options for recovery path
998:   - User confirms which path to take
999:   - Agent follows confirmed path
1000: Validation: Recovery is user-directed, not agent-determined
1001: ```
1002: 
1003: ## 7.2 Non-Breaking Criteria
1004: 
1005: | Criterion | Validation Method |
1006: |-----------|------------------|
1007: | No ceremony added to workflows | User confirms no ritual overhead |
1008: | Existing test suite passes | `npm test` clean |
1009: | Build succeeds | `npm run build` clean |
1010: | Context rot defense doesn't block | Direct action test passes |
1011: | Verification gates user-controlled | Gates at user points, not ritual |
1012: | No framework dogma | Multiple framework awareness works |
1013: 
1014: ## 7.3 Regression Prevention
1015: 
1016: 1. **Pre-commit checks:**
1017:    ```bash
1018:    npm run build
1019:    npm run lint:boundary
1020:    npm test
1021:    ```
1022: 
1023: 2. **Skill loading validation:**
1024:    - Context-intelligence skill loads on session start
1025:    - Subskills load on correct triggers
1026:    - No circular dependencies
1027: 
1028: 3. **Integration tests:**
1029:    - Workflows execute without ceremony overhead
1030:    - Framework selection is situational, not naming-based
1031:    - Multi-framework awareness works
1032:    - User verification gates respected
1033: 
1034: ---
1035: 
1036: # 8. IMPLEMENTATION PHASES
1037: 
1038: ## Phase 1: Core Entry Pack (This Planning Document)
1039: - Create `skills/context-intelligence/SKILL.md`
1040: - Create `skills/context-intelligence/references/`
1041: - Validate non-breaking integration
1042: 
1043: ## Phase 2: Context Rot Model
1044: - Implement detection signals

1046: - Create recovery protocols
1047: 
1048: ## Phase 3: Subskill Branching

1052: 
1053: ## Phase 4: Meta-Builder

1056: - Packaging patterns
1057: 
1058: ## Phase 5: Integration & Testing
1059: - Full test suite
1060: - Non-breaking validation
1061: - User acceptance
1062: 
1063: ---
1064: 
1065: # 9. DEPENDENCIES & CONSTRAINTS
1066: 
1067: ## Dependencies
1068: - OpenCode SDK available (for `client.*` APIs)
1069: - Skills system functional
1070: - Available frameworks (multiple, situational selection)
1071: 
1072: ## Constraints
1073: - Must not break existing mechanisms
1074: - Must not add ceremony to workflows
1075: - Must not force single-framework dogma
1076: - Verification gates must be user-controlled, not ritual
1077: - Framework selection must follow situation, not naming conventions
1078: 
1079: ---
1080:

1082: 
1083: | Metric | Target |

1089: | User verification gate compliance | > 95% |
1090: | Multi-framework situational awareness | > 90% |

144:     - The same issues with communicative and instructive - GPT-5.4 is concise-favor but if the language is not informative enough, other models may not complete the tasks
145: 
146: ---
147:

<path>/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/docs/skill-revamp/architecture.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>1: # Skill Revamp Architecture
2: 
3: **Last updated:** 2026-03-19  
4: **Status:** Planning architecture
5: 
6: ## 1. Mission
7: 
8: The revamp needs a skill-pack architecture that handles:
9: 
10: - front-facing entry complexity
11: - delegated subagent scope
12: - long-session drift
13: - context rot and governance pollution
14: - mixed platform surfaces such as `.opencode`, `.claude`, `.codex`, `.agent`, and others
15: 
16: without turning the pack system into another bloated governance layer.
17: 
18: ## 2. Three-Pattern Model
19: 
20: ### Pattern 1: High-Level Routing
21: 
22: | Property | Decision |
23: |----------|----------|
24: | Role | Must-load entry frame |
25: | Current pack | `context-intelligence` |
26: | Shape | Thin `SKILL.md`, deeper references only on demand |
27: 
28: Pattern 1 decides what kind of session this is before deeper packs load.
29: 
30: ### Pattern 2: Domain And Classification
31: 
32: | Property | Decision |
33: |----------|----------|
34: | Role | Narrow the work once the situation is known |
35: | Example branches | delegation, workflow coordination, AGENTS maintenance |
36: | Shape | Mid-depth references, templates, and bounded guidance |
37: 
38: ### Pattern 3: Specialist Depth
39: 
40: | Property | Decision |
41: |----------|----------|
42: | Role | Deep expertise for fragile situations |
43: | Example branches | recovery, pack migration, audit harnesses |
44: | Shape | Specialist guidance only after Pattern 1 or 2 has narrowed the problem |
45: 
46: ## 3. Session Taxonomy
47: 
48: | Session | Why it matters |
49: |---------|----------------|
50: | Fresh | Entry should stay broad and simple |
51: | Resumed | Prior state may be stale or incomplete |
52: | Delegated | Scope must be explicit and bounded |
53: | Degraded | Drift or context loss is already visible |
54: | Interrupted | Partial actions or incomplete thought chains may exist |
55: | Recovered | Rebuilt state must be re-anchored before specialist depth loads |
56: 
57: ## 4. Context Rot Architecture
58: 
59: Context rot is treated as a structural risk, not a stylistic one.
60: 
61: ### Rot Dimensions
62: 
63: | Dimension | Meaning |
64: |-----------|---------|
65: | Governance ambiguity | Multiple surfaces competing as authority |
66: | Deterministic enforcement | Tests, scripts, hooks, or configs pushing wrong behavior |
67: | Load pressure | Auto-loaded or apparently mandatory surfaces |
68: | Action enablement | Ability of bad context to trigger wrong writes or delegation |
69: | Propagation breadth | How many layers inherit the bad signal |
70: | Freshness and time conflict | Same-level entities disagree and one may be stale |
71: 
72: ### Response Posture
73: 
74: - Low-risk sessions stay broad and lightweight.
75: - Suspect sessions load recovery references before specialist packs.
76: - High-risk sessions favor stop-and-confirm for high-impact actions.
77: 
78: ## 5. Degree Of Freedom
79: 
80: | Level | When to use it | Example |
81: |-------|----------------|---------|
82: | High | Multiple paths are valid | entry framing, principle-driven routing |
83: | Medium | Preferred patterns exist but adaptation is normal | workflow and delegation branches |
84: | Low | Fragile or high-cost errors | naming rules, evaluation rules, packaging rules |
85: 
86: ## 6. Pack Boundary
87: 
88: | Pack | Boundary |
89: |------|----------|
90: | `context-intelligence` | must-load entry defense and routing only |
91: | companion pack | authoring, auditing, packaging, and later migration control |
92: 
93: The companion pack should help create and assess HiveMind packs, but it should not replace Pack 1.
94: 
95: ## 7. Package Shape
96: 
97: ```text
98: skill-name/
99: ├── SKILL.md
100: ├── references/
101: ├── scripts/
102: ├── templates/ or assets/ when justified
103: └── optional examples only when they reduce ambiguity
104: ```
105: 
106: ### Rules
107: 
108: - `SKILL.md` carries the broad workflow and selection logic.
109: - `references/` holds the depth.
110: - `scripts/` should default to discovery and exploration.
111: - reference depth stays one level from `SKILL.md`.
112: 
113: ## 8. Cross-Framework Stance
114: 
115: - `.opencode` is primary for this project but not the only surface agents may see.
116: - `.hivemind` and `dist` are generated or runtime surfaces, not authoring truth.
117: - Root and nested governance docs should be judged by scope, freshness, and real authority.
118: - Cross-framework references are inputs, not automatic instructions.
119: 
120: ## 9. Anti-Patterns
121: 
122: - one giant master skill
123: - duplicated pack roles
124: - entry packs that become procedural ceremonies
125: - specialist packs loaded by default
126: - references that chain into other references
127: 
128: ## 10. External Pattern Anchors
129: 
130: This architecture intentionally draws on live skill-authoring patterns validated during planning:
131: 
132: - Vercel Labs `skill-creator`
133: - Softaworks `skill-judge`
134: - Obra `writing-skills`
135: - Anthropic `skill-creator`
136: 
137: These guide the architecture, but HiveMind-specific boundaries remain local.

(End of file - total 137 lines)
</content>
```

19:

22: - Prefer role or problem nouns over generic verbs.
23: - Do not let aliases become separate physical packs.
24: - Freeze one canonical pack id once the companion pack cycle is approved.
25: 
26: ## 4. Naming Anti-Patterns
27: 
28: - duplicate names for the same pack
29: - giant umbrella names that hide the pack’s job
30: - framework-copy names brought in without adaptation
31: - names that imply authority the pack does not actually own
32: 
33: ## 5. Branch Framing Rule
34: 
35: The pack system should widen by branch, not by stacking more and more meaning into one name. When a new role appears, give it a new branch only if it has a distinct boundary.

<type>file</type>
<content>1: ---
2: name: hivemind-skill-writer
3: description: Use when creating, auditing, refactoring, or packaging HiveMind framework skills. Activates the meta-builder for skill authoring, TDD workflows, and quality validation. Bundles skill-writing guidance, Skill-Judge metrics, and HiveMind-specific packaging patterns. Triggers: "write a skill", "create a new skill", "audit this skill", "is this skill good", "skill quality", "skill design", "skill authoring".
4: version: 1.0.0
5: framework: hivemind
6: pack: hivemind-skill-writer
7: entry-level: L1
8: pattern: P1
9: stacking: 0
10: owner: hivemind
11: status: active
12: tags: [meta, skill-authoring, skill-quality, tdd, hivemind]
13: ---
14: 
15: # hivemind-skill-writer
16: 
17: ## Purpose
18: 
19: Meta-builder skill for authoring HiveMind-specific skills. Use when creating, auditing, refactoring, or packaging skills for the HiveMind ecosystem.
20: 
21: ## When to Activate
22: 
23: **Primary Triggers (answer WHAT + WHEN + KEYWORDS):**
24: - "create a new skill"
25: - "write a skill for..."
26: - "audit this skill"
27: - "is this skill good"
28: - "skill quality check"
29: - "skill design"
30: - "skill authoring"
31: - "refactor this skill"
32: - "package this skill set"
33: 
34: **Secondary Triggers:**
35: - Detecting skill quality issues
36: - Identifying skill redundancy
37: - Planning skill migration
38: 
39: ## Core Philosophy
40: 
41: ### The Iron Law
42: 
43: > **NO SKILL WITHOUT A FAILING TEST FIRST**
44: 
45: Every skill must be validated against a real failure scenario before being written.
46: 
47: ### Knowledge Delta (The Core Formula)
48: 
49: > **Good Skill = Expert-only Knowledge − What Claude Already Knows**
50: 
51: A Skill's value is measured by its **knowledge delta** — the gap between what it provides and what the model already knows.
52: 
53: | Knowledge Type | Definition | Treatment |
54: |---------------|------------|-----------|
55: | **Expert** | Claude genuinely doesn't know this | MUST keep — this is the Skill's value |
56: | **Activation** | Claude knows but may not think of | Keep if brief — serves as reminder |
57: | **Redundant** | Claude definitely knows this | DELETE — wastes tokens |
58: 
59: **Evaluation**: For each section, ask "Does Claude already know this?"
60: 
61: ### Tool vs Skill
62: 
63: | Concept | Essence | Function |
64: |---------|---------|----------|
65: | **Tool** | What model CAN do | Execute actions (bash, read_file, write_file) |
66: | **Skill** | What model KNOWS how to do | Guide decisions (PDF processing, MCP building, frontend design) |
67: 
68: **Equation:** `General Agent + Excellent Skill = Domain Expert Agent`
69: 
70: ### The 5 Patterns System
71: 
72: | Pattern | ~Lines | Purpose | When to Use |
73: |---------|--------|---------|--------------|
74: | **Mindset** | ~50 | Thinking > technique, strong NEVER list | Creative tasks requiring taste |
75: | **Navigation** | ~30 | Minimal SKILL.md, routes to sub-files | Multiple distinct scenarios |
76: | **Philosophy** | ~150 | Philosophy → Express, emphasizes craft | Art/creation requiring originality |
77: | **Process** | ~200 | Phased workflow, checkpoints | Complex multi-step projects |
78: | **Tool** | ~300 | Decision trees, code examples | Precise operations on specific formats |
79: 
80: ### Progressive Disclosure
81: 
82: | Level | Content | When |
83: |-------|---------|------|
84: | **L1** | Metadata (name + description) | Always loaded (~100 tokens) |
85: | **L2** | SKILL.md body | On trigger match (~500 lines) |
86: | **L3** | references/, scripts/, templates/ | Explicit request |
87: 
88: ### Description — THE MOST IMPORTANT FIELD
89: 
90: The description determines if a skill ever gets activated. It MUST answer:
91: 
92: 1. **WHAT**: What does this Skill do?
93: 2. **WHEN**: In what situations should it be used?
94: 3. **KEYWORDS**: What terms should trigger this Skill?
95: 
96: ```
97: ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
98: │  SKILL ACTIVATION FLOW                                              │
99: │                                                                     │
100: │  User Request → Agent sees ALL skill descriptions → Decides which   │
101: │                 (only descriptions, not bodies!)      to activate    │
102: │                                                                     │
103: │  If description doesn't match → Skill NEVER gets loaded            │
104: │  If description is vague → Skill might not trigger when it should  │
105: └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
106: ```
107: 
108: **Excellent description format:**
109: ```yaml
110: description: >
111:   Create, edit, and analyze .docx files. 
112:   Use when working with Word documents, tracked changes, 
113:   or professional document formatting.
114:   Triggers: .docx, tracked changes, Word documents, document editing
115: ```
116: 
117: ### Freedom Calibration
118: 
119: Match specificity to task fragility:
120: 
121: | Task Type | Freedom | Why |
122: |-----------|---------|-----|
123: | Creative/Design | HIGH | Multiple valid approaches, differentiation is value |
124: | Code review | MEDIUM | Principles exist but judgment required |
125: | Precise operations | LOW | One wrong byte corrupts file, consistency critical |
126: 
127: ### TDD Workflow (RED-GREEN-REFACTOR)
128: 
129: **RED Phase:**
130: 1. Identify the failing scenario
131: 2. Write test prompt for the scenario
132: 3. Run without skill — observe failure
133: 4. Document exact failure mode
134: 
135: **GREEN Phase:**
136: 1. Write minimal skill addressing failure
137: 2. Run with skill — observe pass
138: 3. Verify failure mode resolved
139: 4. Document success criteria
140: 
141: **REFACTOR Phase:**
142: 1. Remove duplication
143: 2. Tighten trigger accuracy
144: 3. Ensure reference depth compliance
145: 4. Validate stacking ≤3
146: 
147: ## Skill-Judge Quality Metrics (120 points)
148: 
149: | Dimension | Max | Focus |
150: |-----------|-----|-------|
151: | **D1: Knowledge Delta** | 20 | Expert knowledge not in model |
152: | **D2: Mindset + Procedures** | 15 | Thinking patterns + domain workflows |
153: | **D3: Anti-Pattern Quality** | 15 | Specific NEVER lists with WHY |
154: | **D4: Spec Compliance** | 15 | Description = WHAT + WHEN + KEYWORDS |
155: | **D5: Progressive Disclosure** | 15 | Layering with triggers |
156: | **D6: Freedom Calibration** | 15 | Match specificity to fragility |
157: | **D7: Pattern Recognition** | 10 | Follows established pattern |
158: | **D8: Practical Usability** | 15 | Decision trees, fallbacks, edge cases |
159: 
160: ### Scoring
161: 
162: | Grade | Percentage | Meaning |
163: |-------|------------|---------|
164: | **A** | 90%+ (108+) | Excellent — production-ready |
165: | **B** | 80-89% (96-107) | Good — minor improvements |
166: | **C** | 70-79% (84-95) | Adequate — clear improvement path |
167: | **D** | 60-69% (72-83) | Below average — significant issues |
168: | **F** | <60% (<72) | Poor — fundamental redesign needed |
169: 
170: ### Quality Thresholds
171: 
172: | Score | Grade | Action |
173: |-------|-------|--------|
174: | 4.5+ | EXCELLENT | Ready for release |
175: | 4.0+ | GOOD | Minor improvements |
176: | 3.0+ | ACCEPTABLE | Address gaps |
177: | <3.0 | NEEDS WORK | Major revision required |
178: 
179: ## Context-Intelligence Integration
180: 
181: Every skill must integrate with context-intelligence:
182: 
183: - **Entry State Recognition**: Acknowledge session state
184: - **Trust Threshold**: Know minimum trust scores
185: - **Rot Detection**: Watch for degradation signals
186: - **Recovery Awareness**: Know when to escalate
187: 
188: ## Stacking Discipline
189: 
190: At entry, max **3 skills** may load:
191: 
192: ```
193: context-intelligence (1) — always
194: delegation-scope (1) — if delegated
195: workflow-hierarchy (1) — if workflow
196: context-rot-recovery (1) — if degraded
197: ```
198: 
199: **hivemind-skill-writer does not count** against stack (stacking: 0).
200: 
201: ## NEVER Do
202: 
203: - **NEVER** explain what Claude already knows ("what is X", "how to write a for-loop")
204: - **NEVER** give high scores for well-formatted but redundant content
205: - **NEVER** let length impress you — a 50-line Skill can outperform 500-line
206: - **NEVER** forgive vague descriptions — poor description = skill never triggers
207: - **NEVER** put "when to use" only in body — description is what Agent sees first
208: - **NEVER** skip mentally testing decision trees
209: 
210: ## References
211: 
212: - `references/01-skill-anatomy.md` — Full anatomy template
213: - `references/02-frontmatter-standard.md` — YAML schema
214: - `references/03-three-patterns.md` — Pattern system (HiveMind + Skill-Judge)
215: - `references/04-tdd-workflow.md` — TDD methodology
216: - `references/05-skill-quality-matrix.md` — Skill-Judge metrics (120-point system)
217: - `references/06-knowledge-delta.md` — Expert vs Redundant vs Activation
218: 

(End of file - total 218 lines)
</content>
```
